Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Preemption with Deferred Payment: Hanafi vs. Zufar/Shafi'i
Dispute between Hanafis and Zufar/Shafi'i on preemptor taking property with deferred payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a preemptor taking property with deferred payment, explain why ajal is not a description, and compare it with the opposing view.

Core Idea
The term (ajal) is a condition, not a description; the preemptor cannot take with deferred payment.

When a property is sold on deferred payment, the preemptor may want to exercise his right of preemption. But can he take the property on the same deferred terms? The Hanafi school says no – he must pay immediately or wait. This lesson examines the reasoning behind this ruling and the disagreement with Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i (old opinion).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed point
Recognize that the issue is: after a sale with deferred payment, the preemptor claims shuf'ah. Can he take the property with the same deferred payment?
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its two options
The preemptor can either pay the full price immediately and take the property now, or wait until the term expires and then pay. He cannot take immediately with deferred payment.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
3
Examine the opposing view's analogy
Zufar and Shafi'i (old) argue that ajal is a description of the price, like counterfeitness. Just as the preemptor must accept counterfeit dirhams if the sale was for them, he must accept deferral.
They treat ajal as a wasf that follows the price.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis respond: ajal is a condition (shart) established by agreement, not a description. It is the buyer's right, not the seller's. Consent for the buyer does not imply consent for the preemptor. They analogize to bay' al-tawliyah: deferral does not transfer without explicit mention.
The key distinction: condition vs. description; consent is person-specific.

گیا کیونکہ لوگوں کے احوال مختلف ہیں کہ کوئی نادہندہ ہے اور کوئی دہندہ
If he sells with deferred payment, the preemptor has the option: if he wishes, he takes it with immediate payment; if he wishes, he waits until the term expires then takes it. He does not have the right to take it immediately with deferred payment. Zufar said he has that (right), and that is the old opinion of al-Shafi'i, because being deferred is a description (wasf) of the price, like being counterfeit. And taking by preemption, he takes it with its origin and its description, as in counterfeit dirhams. Translation: Al-Quduri said: When he sells with deferred payment, the preemptor has the choice: he may take it with prompt payment, or he may wait until the term expires and then take it. He does not have the right to take it immediately with deferred payment. Zufar said he has that right, and that is the old opinion of al-Shafi'i, because being deferred is a description of the price like counterfeit, and taking by preemption, he takes it with its origin and description as in counterfeit dirhams. Explanation: The seller sold his house to the buyer for, say, two thousand rupees, and payment was deferred. The preemptor claimed preemption. Now the question: if the preemptor takes it, will he take it for the same two thousand but pay now, or will the same payment time be fixed? There is disagreement. The opinion of Imam Zufar and the old opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i is that the price is also deferred for the preemptor; thus payment is not immediate but on the fixed time. They said: Just as counterfeitness is a description of dirhams, so here the term (ajal) is a description of the price. So if the seller sold the house for counterfeit dirhams, the preemptor has the right to give those same counterfeit dirhams and take the house. Similarly here, the preemptor has the right to take the house in exchange for the deferred price. In summary, they considered the term a description of the price, and the description follows the described. So when the price becomes due on the preemptor, it will be with its description. This concludes the evidence of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i's old opinion. Next, the author presents his evidence, saying: Our evidence is that the term is established by condition, and there is no condition between the preemptor and the seller or buyer. And the seller's consent to deferment for the buyer is not consent to deferment for the preemptor because people differ in wealth. And the term is not a description of the price, because it is the right of the buyer. If it were a description, it would follow the price, and then it would be a right of the seller, like the price itself. This is like when someone buys something with deferred payment and then does a sale of assignment (tawliyah) to another, the term is not established unless mentioned. Similarly here. Translation: Our evidence is that the term (ajal) is established by condition, and there is no condition between the preemptor and the seller or buyer. And the seller's consent to it for the buyer is not consent to it for the preemptor because people differ in financial capacity. And the term is not a description of the price, because it is the right of the buyer. If it were a description of the price, it would follow the price, and then it would be the right of the seller, like the price itself. This is like when someone buys something with deferred payment and then assigns it (tawliyah) to another, the term is not established without explicit mention. Explanation: This is our evidence: ajal is not a description; it is established by condition. The condition is between seller and buyer, not between preemptor and seller or preemptor and buyer. And the seller's willingness to give deferred payment to the buyer does not imply willingness to give it to the preemptor, because people's circumstances differ: one may be insolvent and another wealthy.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. The issue: when a property is sold with a deferred payment (thaman mu'ajjal), can the preemptor (shafī') take the property immediately by paying the full price in cash, or must he match the deferred payment terms? The Hanafi position (from Al-Quduri and the majority of Hanafis, including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) is that the preemptor has two options: (1) pay the full price immediately in cash and take the property, or (2) wait until the term expires and then pay. He cannot take the property immediately with a deferred payment because the term is a condition agreed between the seller and buyer only. Zufar (a Hanafi scholar who sometimes differs) and Imam al-Shafi'i (in his old opinion) argue that the preemptor can take the property with the same deferred payment, because they consider the term (ajal) to be a description (wasf) of the price, like counterfeitness. Therefore, just as the preemptor must take the price with its description (e.g., counterfeit dirhams), he must also take it with the term. The Hanafis respond with a rational argument: ajal is not a description but a condition (shart) that arises from agreement between seller and buyer. There is no such agreement with the preemptor. Additionally, ajal is the buyer's right (to delay payment), not the seller's or the price's. If it were a description, it would belong to the price and thus be the seller's right, but it is not. They analogize to bay' al-tawliyah (sale at cost with assignment): if someone buys with deferred payment and then assigns the sale to another (tawliyah), the assignment does not automatically include the deferral unless explicitly mentioned. Similarly, shuf'ah does not include the deferral. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view: the preemptor must pay immediately or wait; he cannot take with deferred payment without the seller's consent.

Key Terms
ثمن مؤجل (thaman mu'ajjal): Deferred price; payment is delayed to a future date.
اجل (ajal): Term, period of deferment; the agreed future time for payment.
وصف (wasf): Description or attribute; here refers to whether ajal is an attribute of the price itself.
بیع تولیہ (bay' al-tawliyah): Sale at cost price; a transaction where the buyer assigns the purchase to another at the same price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a house is sold with a one-year deferred payment, what is the preemptor's option?
A) He must pay the full price immediately and take the house
B) He can take the house and pay after one year
C) He has the choice to pay immediately now or wait one year and then pay
D) He can only take the house after one year by paying then

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between a condition (ajal) and a description (wasf); the preemptor's right does not include the buyer's agreement to defer payment.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Immediate Demand for Pre-emption Upon Knowledge of Sale: Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the ruling on immediate demand for pre-emption and intra-Hanafi difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing of talab and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad from Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Demand for pre-emption must be immediate; silence upon knowledge voids the right.

Pre-emption (shuf'ah) is a right to step into a sale of jointly owned property. Upon learning of a sale, the pre-emptor must assert this right immediately. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement about what happens if the pre-emptor remains silent without making an immediate demand. This lesson clarifies the positions and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The question is whether the pre-emptor is required to make a verbal demand (talab) immediately upon knowledge of the sale, or whether he can delay it. The matn seems to allow waiting, but the Hidayah clarifies this refers to taking, not demand.
The phrase 'if he wishes to wait' in the matn applies to the act of taking (akhdh), not the demand (talab).
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, demand must be made immediately. If the pre-emptor remains silent without demanding, his right of pre-emption is void. Their evidence: the right is established by the sale, and the pre-emptor can take immediately by paying the price, so silence indicates aversion.
This is the majority view and the mufta bihi.
3
Explain Abu Yusuf's later opinion
Abu Yusuf's later opinion holds that the pre-emptor's silence does not void his right. His evidence: demand itself is not the goal; taking is. Since the pre-emptor may not have the price ready, his silence does not necessarily show abandonment.
Abu Yusuf initially agreed with the majority but later changed his view.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. In practice, a pre-emptor must make an immediate demand upon learning of the sale; failure to do so will likely lead to losing the right, though some judges may consider the minority view.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah adopts the majority view.

كتاب الشفعة
قوله وان شاء صبرتم ينقضی الاجل عبارت کی وضاحت
وقوله في الكتاب وان شاء صحيحة ينقضى الاحل مراده الصبر عن الأخذ اما الطلب عليه في الحال حتى لو سكت عنه الطلب شفعته عند ابي حنيفه ومحمد حلا فالقول ابى يوسف الاخر لان حق الشفعة انما يثبت بالبيع والاخذ يتراخى عن الطلب وهو متكن من الاخذ فى الحال بان يؤدى الثمن حالا فيشترط الطلب عند العلم بالبيع
ترجمہ اور تقول لقد ورثی کا کتاب میں و ان شاء صبح ينقضى الاجل اس کی مراد لینے سے صبر کرنا ہے۔ بہر حال طلب فی الحال ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر اس نے طلب سے سکوت کیا تو اس کا شفعہ باطل ہو جائے گا یا ابوحنیفہ اور محمد کے نزدیک بخلاف ابو یوسف کے آخری قول کے ۔ اسلئے کہ شفعہ کا حق بیع سے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے اور لینا طلب سے موخر ہو جاتا ہے اور وہ فی الحال لینے پر قادر ہے۔ اس طرح کہ یمن [؟] نقد ادا کر دے تو بیع کے علم کے وقت طلب شرط ہے۔ تشریح صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ متن میں جو آیا تھا وان شاء صبحتى [؟] ينقضى الاجل اس کا مطلب یہ نہ سمجھ لینا کہ شفیع کو حق ہے کہ مدت گذرنے تک طلب شفعہ سے صبر کرے بلکہ طلب تو بیع کا علم ہوتے ہی کرنی پڑے گی۔ ورنہ حضرات طرفین کے زند یک [؟] شفعہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔
البتہ امام ابو یوسف کا آخری قول ہے کہ شفعہ باطل نہیں ہو گا۔ امام ابو یوسف پہلے وہی فرماتے تھے جو طرفین فرماتے تھے بلکہ مطلب یہ ہے کہ لینے سے صبر کر سکتا ہے رہی طلب و ہ فی الحال کرنی پڑے گی۔
امام قدوری کے قول کی تشریح ہوگئی اب فریقین کے دلائل سنے۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل مصنف نے بیان نہیں کی بہر حال امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلب شفعہ بذات خود مقصود نہیں بلکہ لینا مقصود ہے اور وہ لینے پر فی الحال قادر نہیں تو پھر اس کی طلب سے ابھی کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ لہذا فی الحال اس کا سکوت اعراض کی دلیل نہیں بنے گا۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ بات تو مسلم ہے کہ بیچ ہوتے ہی شفعہ میں طلب واجب ہوتی ہے رہا مسئلہ لینے کا تو طلب اور اخذ میں کبھی فصل ہو جاتا ہے جس کے بہت سے شواہدل [؟] سکتے ہیں۔ بہر حال اگر یہ تسلیم کر لیا جائے کہ اخذ ہی شفعہ کا مقصود اصلی ہے تو شفیع فی الحال بھی تو لے سکتا ہے۔ نقد شمن [؟] ادا کرے اور فی الحال لے لے۔ وہ تو شفیع کو ضر ر [؟] سے بچانے کی وجہ سے فی الحال اخذ اس کے اوپر لازم نہیں کیا گیا تو جب فی الحال لینے پر قادر ہے تو حسب سابق طلب فی الحال لازم ہوگی یعنی بیچ کا علم ہوتے ہی طلب شفعہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ ورنہ دلیل اعراض کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے شفعہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔
The Book of Pre-emption. Explanation of the phrase: 'And if he wishes to wait, the term expires.' And his saying in the book: 'And if he wishes [something?] the term expires' means he intends to delay taking, but the demand is immediate. So much so that if he remains silent about the demand, his pre-emption is void according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to the later opinion of Abu Yusuf. Because the right of pre-emption is established by the sale, and taking is postponed beyond demand, and he is able to take immediately by paying the price at once, so demand is required at the time of knowledge of the sale. Translation: And the saying 'and if he wishes ... expires' in the book means he is patient from taking; however, demand is immediate, such that if he remains silent from demand, his pre-emption becomes void according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, unlike Abu Yusuf's later opinion. Because the right of pre-emption is established by the sale, and taking is delayed after demand, and he is able to take immediately, as he pays the price in cash, so demand is a condition at the time of knowledge of the sale. Commentary: The author of Hidayah says that the phrase in the matn 'and if he wishes ... expires' should not be understood as meaning that the pre-emptor has the right to delay demanding pre-emption until the term passes. Rather, demand must be made immediately upon knowledge of the sale. Otherwise, according to the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad], the pre-emption becomes void. However, Imam Abu Yusuf's later opinion is that it does not become void. Imam Abu Yusuf initially held the same opinion as the two, but the meaning is that he can delay taking, but demand must be made immediately. The explanation of Imam Quduri's statement is complete; now hear the evidences of the two parties. The author did not mention Imam Abu Yusuf's evidence. In any case, Imam Abu Yusuf's evidence is that the demand for pre-emption is not intrinsically intended, rather taking is intended, and he is not able to take immediately, so his demand now has no benefit. Therefore, his silence now does not constitute evidence of aversion. The evidence of the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] is that it is agreed that upon sale, demand in pre-emption becomes obligatory. As for the issue of taking, sometimes there is a separation between demand and taking, for which many examples can be given. In any case, if it is accepted that taking is the actual purpose of pre-emption, then the pre-emptor can take immediately; he pays the price in cash and takes immediately. Because he is protected from harm, immediate taking is not made obligatory upon him. So when he is able to take immediately, as previously, demand becomes necessary immediately, i.e., upon knowledge of the sale, making demand for pre-emption is a condition. Otherwise, due to the presence of evidence of aversion, the pre-emption becomes void.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the timing of the demand (talab) for pre-emption (shuf'ah). The author of the Hidayah explains that the matn's phrase 'and if he wishes to wait until the term expires' does not indicate that the pre-emptor may delay the demand; rather, the demand must be made immediately upon learning of the sale. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two shaykhs), if the pre-emptor remains silent without making a demand, his right of pre-emption is void. Abu Yusuf's later opinion holds that it is not void. The reasoning is: the right of pre-emption is established by the sale, and while the actual taking (akhdh) can be delayed after the demand, the demand itself is immediate because the pre-emptor is capable of taking immediately by paying the price. Abu Yusuf argues that since the pre-emptor may not have the price ready, his silence is not necessarily evidence of abandonment; the purpose is taking, not demand itself. The two shaykhs counter that the pre-emptor can take immediately if he wishes, and because the right was given to protect him from harm, he is not forced to take immediately, but demand is still required immediately; otherwise his silence indicates aversion, voiding the right. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, which is the majority view and is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): Right of pre-emption; the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a property sold to a third party under the same terms.
طلب (talab): Demand; the immediate verbal assertion of the right of pre-emption upon knowledge of the sale.
اخذ (akhdh): Taking; the actual acquisition of the property by the pre-emptor after demand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a pre-emptor learns of a sale but does not make an immediate demand, what happens to his right of pre-emption?
A) His right remains valid indefinitely.
B) His right is void.
C) His right is suspended until he pays the price.
D) His right becomes optional.

Key Takeaway
Immediate demand is wajib; silence voids the right per the majority Hanafi view.

Pre-emption When Sale Consideration is Wine or Pork by a Non-Muslim
Ruling on a dhimmi pre-emptor taking property sold for wine or pork

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a pre-emptor's compensation (mithl or qīmah) depends on whether the price is fungible (mithlī) or non-fungible (qīmī) for that pre-emptor, considering his religion.

Core Idea
Pre-emptor gives like of fungible price, value of non-fungible; Muslim always gives value for wine or pork.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario: a house sold by or to a dhimmī in exchange for wine or pork. The pre-emptor may be a dhimmī or a Muslim. The Hanafi school uses the categories of fungible and non-fungible goods to determine the correct compensation, considering the legal capacity of the pre-emptor to possess the price commodity. Understanding this ruling clarifies how shuf‘a rights remain intact even when the consideration is ritually impure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the price
Determine who is the seller, buyer, and pre-emptor. Note whether the pre-emptor is a dhimmī or a Muslim. The price is either wine or pork.
2
Classify the price as fungible or non-fungible for that pre-emptor
For a dhimmī, wine is fungible (like vinegar) and pork is non-fungible (like sheep). For a Muslim, both are non-fungible because he cannot lawfully possess or deliver them.
The illa (effective cause) is the pre-emptor's legal capacity to own and transfer the item.
3
Apply the compensation rule
If the price is fungible for the pre-emptor, he gives the like (mithl). If non-fungible, he gives the value (qīmah). For a dhimmī: like of wine, value of pork. For a Muslim: value of both.
4
Handle mixed pre-emptors or conversion
If one pre-emptor is Muslim and another dhimmī, each takes half with half the compensation appropriate to their status. If a dhimmī pre-emptor converts to Islam, he must now pay the value, because he can no longer lawfully possess wine.
The part follows the whole; conversion does not nullify the right but changes the compensation.
5
Note the underlying principle
The sale is valid among dhimmīs, and the right of shuf‘a is general for Muslims and dhimmīs. The compensation rule follows the nature of the price as determined by the pre-emptor's capacity.
Proof: qiyas (analogy) – wine:dhimmī :: vinegar:Muslim; pork:dhimmī :: sheep:Muslim.

تشریح ایک ذمی کا مکان ہے جس کو دوسرے ذمی نے شراب یا خنزیر کے عوض خرید لیا اور مکان کا شفیع بھی ذمی ہے اور شفعہ مسلمان اور زمی سب کیلئے عام ہے۔ اور ذمیوں کیلئے شراب کا حکم ہمارے لئے بکری کے حکم کے مثل ہے۔ بہر حال ذمی شفیع شراب کی صورت میں شراب کا مثل دے کر اس مکان کو لے لے گا اور خنزیر کی صورت میں خنزیر کی قیمت دے کر لے گا۔ کیونکہ شراب ذوات الامتثال [؟] میں سے اور خنزیر ذوات العقیم [؟] میں سے ہے اور اول میں مثل اور ثانی میں قیمت کا حکم ہوا کرتا ہے۔ شفیع مسلمان ہو تو شراب اور خنزیر کی قیمت دے کر خرید لے
قال وان كان شفيعها مسلما اخذها بقيمة الخمر والخنزير اما الخنزير فظاهر وكذا الخمر لامتناع التسليم والتسلم في حق المسلم فالتحق بغير المثلى
ترجمہ اور اگر دار کا شفیع مسلمان ہو تو شفیع اس کو شراب اور خنزیر کی قیمت کے بدلہ خرید لے گا۔ بہر حال خنزیر پس یہ تو ظاہر ہے اور ایسے ہی شراب تسلیم و تسلیم [؟] کے ممتنع ہونے کی وجہ سے مسلم کے حق میں ۔
تشریح اگر اس گھر کا شفیع مسلمان ہو تو اس کو بھی شفعہ ملے گا لیکن وہ دونوں صورتوں میں شراب یا خنزیر کی قیمت دے گا۔ رہا خنزیر میں قیمت دینا یہ تو ظاہر ہے اور رہا مسئلہ شراب کا تو چونکہ مسلمان شراب پر نہ تو قبضہ کر سکتا ہے اور نہ کر سکتا ہے تو مسلم کے حق میں شراب نیہ مثالی [؟] کے حکم میں ہے تو شراب غیر متلی [؟] ہوگئی اور غیر مشکلی [؟] میں قیمت دی جاتی ہے ا سلئے اس میں بھی قیمت دی جائے گی۔ مذکورہ گھر کے شفیع مسلمان اور ذمی ہوں تو پھر کیا حکم ہے
وان كان شفيعها مسلما وذميا اخذ المسلم نصفها بنصف قيمة الخمر والذمى نصفها بنصف مثل الخمر اعتبار للبعض بالكل فلو اسلم الذمى اخذها بنصف قيمة الخمر بعجزه عن تملیک الخمر وبالاسلام يتاكذ حقه لاان يبطل فصار كما اذا اشتراها بكر من رطب فحضر الشفيع بعد انقطاعه ياخذها بقيمة الرطب كذا هذا
If a house is bought in exchange for wine or pork, and the pre-emptor is a dhimmi, he takes it with the like of wine and the value of pork. He said: And if a dhimmi buys with wine or pork, and its pre-emptor is a dhimmi, he takes it with the like of wine and the value of pork, because this sale is judged valid between them, and the right of pre-emption is general for Muslim and dhimmi, and wine for them is like vinegar for us, and pork for them is like a sheep. So he takes in the first case with the like, and in the second case with the value. Translation: And when a dhimmi buys with wine or pork, and the pre-emptor of that house is a dhimmi, he will take it with the like of wine and the value of pork. Because this transaction is judged valid between them, and the right of pre-emption is common for Muslim and dhimmi. And wine for them is like vinegar for us, and pork for them is like a goat. So the pre-emptor takes in the first case with the like and in the second case with the value. Commentary: A dhimmi owns a house which another dhimmi buys in exchange for wine or pork, and the pre-emptor of the house is also a dhimmi. Pre-emption is general for Muslim and dhimmi. For dhimmis, the ruling of wine is like the ruling of vinegar for us, and pork for them is like a goat for us. So the dhimmi pre-emptor will take the house by giving the like of wine in the case of wine, and by giving the value of pork in the case of pork, because wine is among fungibles and pork is among non-fungibles, and in the first case the ruling is like, in the second case value. If the pre-emptor is a Muslim, he buys it with the value of wine and pork. He said: And if its pre-emptor is a Muslim, he takes it with the value of wine and pork. As for pork, it is apparent; similarly wine due to the impossibility of delivery and receipt for the Muslim, so it is attached to non-fungibles. Translation: And if the pre-emptor of the house is a Muslim, the pre-emptor will buy it in exchange for the value of wine and pork. In any case, pork is apparent, and similarly wine due to the impossibility of delivery and receipt for the Muslim. Commentary: If the pre-emptor of that house is a Muslim, he will also get pre-emption, but he will pay the value of wine or pork in both cases. As for paying value for pork, it is apparent. As for the issue of wine, because a Muslim cannot take possession of or deliver wine, so for the Muslim, wine is considered a non-fungible, so wine becomes a non-fungible, and for non-fungibles, value is given. Therefore, he will also pay value in this case. If the pre-emptors of the mentioned house are a Muslim and a dhimmi, then what is the ruling? And if its pre-emptor is a Muslim and a dhimmi, the Muslim takes half with half the value of wine, and the dhimmi takes half with half the like of wine, considering the part with the whole. If the dhimmi becomes Muslim, he takes it with half the value of wine due to his inability to transfer ownership of wine, and with Islam his right is strengthened, not nullified. So it becomes as if he bought it, like with dates from ripe dates, and the pre-emptor appears after its extinction, he takes it with the value of ripe dates. So also this.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on pre-emption when the sale consideration involves wine or pork and involves dhimmīs and Muslims. The key points: (1) If both buyer and pre-emptor are dhimmīs, the pre-emptor takes the property by giving the like (mithl) of wine if wine was the price, and the value (qīmah) of pork if pork was the price. This is because among dhimmīs, wine is considered a fungible (mithlī) like vinegar for Muslims, and pork is a non-fungible (qīmī) like sheep. (2) If the pre-emptor is a Muslim, he gives the value of both wine and pork, because a Muslim cannot lawfully possess or deliver wine or pork, so they are treated as non-fungibles. (3) If there are two pre-emptors, one Muslim and one dhimmī, the Muslim takes half with half the value of wine, and the dhimmī takes half with half the like of wine. If the dhimmī later converts to Islam, he must pay half the value because he becomes unable to transfer ownership of wine. The ruling is analogous to a case where a pre-emptor appears after the price commodity (e.g., dates) has perished; he then pays its value. The proof is that the sale is considered valid between the dhimmī parties, and the right of pre-emption is general for both Muslims and dhimmīs. The Hanafi school classifies wine for dhimmīs as fungible (like vinegar) and pork as non-fungible (like sheep), relying on the custom and legal capacity of dhimmīs.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim subject of an Islamic state who is protected by a covenant (dhimmah) and allowed to practice his religion.
مثل (mithl): Like; the identical type and quantity of a fungible good, e.g., wine for wine.
قيمة (qīmah): Value; the monetary equivalent of a non-fungible item.
ذوات المثال (dhawāt al-amthal): Fungible items; goods that can be replaced by similar items (e.g., wine, wheat).
ذوات القيمة (dhawāt al-qīmah): Non-fungible items; unique goods where compensation is by value (e.g., pork, sheep).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim is the pre-emptor of a house sold to a dhimmī for wine, how does the Muslim pre-emptor compensate?
A) He gives the like of wine.
B) He gives the value of wine.
C) He gives nothing because the sale is invalid.
D) He gives the like of wine if he is a dhimmī.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi shuf‘a, the pre-emptor must compensate with the like of a fungible price and the value of a non-fungible price, considering the pre-emptor's capacity to lawfully possess the price commodity.

Shuf'ah for Dhimmi Pre-emptor When Dhimmi Buys with Wine or Pig
Ruling for dhimmi pre-emptor when dhimmi buys house with wine or pig

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the method of payment for a dhimmi pre-emptor when a dhimmi buys a house with wine or pig, and explain the legal reasoning based on the validity of the sale among dhimmis.

Core Idea
A dhimmi pre-emptor pays in kind for wine and value for pig because wine is mithli and pig is qimi among them.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in pre-emption (shuf'ah) law: when a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen) purchases a house in exchange for wine or a pig, and another dhimmi seeks to pre-empt that purchase. The Hanafi school, recognising that such a sale is valid between dhimmis, allows the pre-emptor to take the house by paying the same wine (like-for-like) or the value of the pig. This illustrates how Hanafi fiqh respects the legal capacity of non-Muslims in transactions while maintaining the general applicability of shuf'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and transaction
A dhimmi buyer purchased a house, paying with wine or a pig. Another dhimmi is the pre-emptor (shafi'). This sets up the scenario.
2
Determine legal status of the sale among dhimmis
The sale is considered valid between them because wine and pig are lawful for dhimmis. This is the key premise.
Hanafi law respects dhimmi personal law in their own transactions.
3
Classify the consideration as mithli or qimi
Wine is mithli (fungible, like vinegar for Muslims) so it can be paid like-for-like. Pig is non-mithli (qimi) so it must be paid by value.
Mithli goods are measured or weighed; qimi goods are unique or not standardized.
4
Conclude the ruling
The dhimmi pre-emptor takes the house by giving the equivalent wine (for wine payment) or the monetary value of the pig (for pig payment).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا اشترى ذمى بخمر اوخنزير وشفيعها ذمي اخذها بمثل الخمر وقيمة الخنزير لان هذا البيع مقضى بالصحة فيما بينهم وحق الشفعة يعم المسلم والذمى والخمر لهم كالخل لنا ولخنزير كالشاة فياخد في الأول بالمثل والثاني بالقيمة. قال وان كان شفيعها مسلما اخذها بقيمة الخمر والخنزير اما الخنزير فظاهر وكذا الخمر لامتناع التسليم والتسلم في حق المسلم فالتحق بغير المثلى
He said: And if a dhimmi buys with wine or pig, and its pre-emptor is a dhimmi, he takes it with the like of the wine and the value of the pig, because this sale is judged as valid between them, and the right of pre-emption is general for Muslim and dhimmi; and wine for them is like vinegar for us, and pig for them is like a sheep. So he takes in the first case with the like, and in the second with the value. He said: And if its pre-emptor is a Muslim, he takes it with the value of the wine and the pig. As for the pig, it is obvious, and likewise the wine because of the impossibility of delivery and receipt in the case of the Muslim, so it becomes like a non-mithli.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on pre-emption (shuf'ah) when a dhimmi buys a house in exchange for wine or a pig. The text presents two scenarios: first, when the pre-emptor is also a dhimmi, he can take the house by giving the same wine (like for like) or the value of the pig. The reasoning is that among dhimmis, such a sale is valid, and wine and pig are considered lawful commodities for them – like vinegar or a sheep for Muslims. So the dhimmi pre-emptor pays in kind for wine and in monetary value for the pig (since pigs are not measured by like). Second, if the pre-emptor is a Muslim, he must pay the market value of both wine and pig because a Muslim cannot legally possess or deliver wine or pig. Hence, they are treated as non-mithli (goods not of the same kind), and the pre-emptor pays their value. This shows the Hanafi principle that shuf'ah is general for all, but the method of payment adapts to what is lawful for the pre-emptor.

Key Terms
شفعة (Shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption; a legal right for a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold property under certain conditions.
مثل (Mithl): The exact equivalent in kind (like for like), used for goods that are measured or weighed (mithliyyat).
قيمة (Qimah): Market value (price) of a good, used when the good is non-mithli or cannot be lawfully delivered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because pig is mithli
B) Because pig is qimi
C) Because the pre-emptor is a Muslim
D) Because the sale is invalid

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi pre-emptor pays in kind for wine (mithli) and value for pig (qimi) because the sale is valid among dhimmis.

Shuf'ah for Muslim Pre-emptor When Dhimmi Buys with Wine or Pig
Ruling for Muslim pre-emptor when dhimmi buys house with wine or pig

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why a Muslim pre-emptor must pay the value (qimah) of wine or pig, and explain the principle of impossibility of lawful delivery.

Core Idea
A Muslim pre-emptor pays market value for wine and pig because he cannot lawfully possess or deliver these items.

This lesson examines the second scenario from the Hidayah passage: when a dhimmi buys a house with wine or pig, but the pre-emptor is a Muslim. The Hanafi ruling mandates that the Muslim pre-emptor pay the monetary value (qimah) of both the wine and the pig. The reasoning is that a Muslim cannot legally deliver or receive wine or pig, so they are treated as non-mithli goods. This highlights how Islamic legal capacity and prohibitions affect the application of shuf'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
A dhimmi buyer purchased a house with wine or pig. The pre-emptor is a Muslim.
2
Recognize the prohibition
A Muslim cannot lawfully possess, deliver, or receive wine or pig. These are haram for him.
3
Apply the rule of impossibility
Since the Muslim pre-emptor cannot take the same wine (mithl) or pig, both become non-mithli (qimi). Therefore, he must pay the market value.
For pig, it is obvious because pig is already qimi; for wine, the impossibility of lawful delivery renders it qimi.
4
Conclude the ruling
The Muslim pre-emptor pays the value (qimah) of both the wine and the pig.

Mixed Pre-emptors: Muslim and Dhimmi After Wine Purchase
Ruling with proof via qiyas to ripe dates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for joint pre-emptors of differing religion when the consideration is wine, and explain the qiyas to the ripe dates case.

Core Idea
Pre-emptors keep their right after conversion; payment adjusts to value when the consideration becomes unlawful.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario: a house purchased with wine has two co-pre-emptors, one Muslim and one dhimmi. The Hanafi school rules that each takes his share, but the Muslim cannot take wine so he pays its value. If the dhimmi later becomes Muslim, his right remains, and he too pays value. The ruling is justified by a qiyas to the case of ripe dates that become unavailable. We will unpack the ruling, the analogy, and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the consideration
Note that the house was bought with wine (khamr), and there are two pre-emptors: a Muslim and a dhimmi. The Muslim cannot lawfully accept wine, so his payment must be different from the dhimmi's.
The dhimmi can lawfully possess wine, so he pays with wine itself.
2
Determine each pre-emptor's payment
The Muslim takes his half by paying half the value (qimat) of the wine. The dhimmi takes his half by paying half the like (mithl) of the wine – i.e., actual wine.
The maxim 'i'tibar al-ba'd bi-al-kull' is applied: the ruling for a half-share is the same as for the full share.
3
Analyze the effect of the dhimmi's conversion to Islam
If the dhimmi becomes Muslim before taking his share, he can no longer take wine. The text states his right is strengthened, not annulled, so he now pays the value of the wine.
Conversion does not void the shuf'ah right; it only changes the mode of payment.
4
Trace the qiyas to the ripe dates case
The ruling is analogized to a scenario where a house is bought with ripe dates (rutab) that are out of season by the time the pre-emptor appears. The pre-emptor pays the value of the dates. Similarly here, the converted pre-emptor cannot get the wine, so he pays its value.
The illa (effective cause) is the inability to lawfully deliver/possess the specific commodity.
5
Apply the ruling to similar scenarios
Use the reasoning to derive rulings for other cases where the consideration becomes unavailable or unlawful for the pre-emptor after the sale.
Extension: if the consideration is pork and the pre-emptor converts, same rule applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان شفيعها مسلما وذميا اخذ المسلم نصفها بنصف قيمة الخمر والذمى نصفها بنصف مثل الخمر اعتبار للبعض بالكل فلو اسلم الذمى اخذها بنصف قيمة الخمر بعجزه عن تملیک الخمر وبالاسلام يتاكذ حقه لاان يبطل فصار كما اذا اشتراها بكر من رطب فحضر الشفيع بعد انقطاعه ياخذها بقيمة الرطب كذا هذا
And if its pre-emptor is a Muslim and a dhimmi, the Muslim takes half of it with half the value of the wine, and the dhimmi takes half of it with half the like of the wine, considering the part as the whole. So if the dhimmi becomes Muslim, he takes it with half the value of the wine due to his inability to give ownership of wine, and by Islam his right is strengthened, not annulled. So it becomes like when one buys it with a measure of ripe dates, and the pre-emptor appears after they are out of season, he takes it with the value of the ripe dates. Similarly this.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling for a scenario where a house is bought with wine and two co-pre-emptors exist: one Muslim and one dhimmi. The ruling is that each takes half the property proportionally. The Muslim pays half the market value of the wine (since he cannot take the wine itself), and the dhimmi pays half the actual wine (like for like, as wine is permissible for him). The principle is 'considering the part as the whole' – i.e., the same rule applies to the half as to the full. Then the text addresses a change: if the dhimmi later becomes Muslim before taking, he then takes his half (or the whole if he is the only one) by paying half the value of the wine, because he can no longer lawfully receive wine. His right is not voided by conversion; rather, it is affirmed, so he pays value. This is analogized to a case where a house is bought with fresh dates that later become unavailable; the pre-emptor pays the value. Thus, the Hanafi school shows flexibility in adapting payment to the pre-emptor's legal status at the time of taking.

Key Terms
شمول (Shumul): Generality: the right of shuf'ah applies to all pre-emptors regardless of religion.
اعتبار البعض بالكل (I'tibar al-ba'd bi-al-kull): Legal maxim: The ruling for a part is same as for the whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) With half the value of the wine
C) With cash only
D) He does not pay

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah applies even when the consideration is non-Islamic; payment adapts to the pre-emptor's legal capacity at the time of taking, as shown by the qiyas to ripe dates.

Pre-emptor's Option When Buyer Improves Property
Ruling on pre-emptor's option after buyer's improvements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to a pre-emptor when the buyer has built or planted on the property and explain the legal basis for each option.

Core Idea
Pre-emptor chooses: pay for improvements or force removal.

This lesson examines a critical scenario in pre-emption (shuf'ah): what happens when the buyer has added improvements to the property before the pre-emptor exercises his right? The Hanafi school gives the pre-emptor a powerful choice: either take the property together with the improvements by paying their value, or force the buyer to remove them at his own expense. This rule balances the pre-emptor's right to reclaim his share with fairness to the buyer who invested in the property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling context
Recognize that this is a ruling on pre-emption (shuf'ah) after a sale, where the buyer has made physical changes (building or planting) to the land before the pre-emptor asserts his right.
The pre-emptor's right vests at the time of sale, but the buyer's improvements create a new situation.
2
List the two options
From the text, extract the two choices: (1) take the property by paying the original sale price plus the current value of the improvements, or (2) compel the buyer to remove the improvements at the buyer's expense.
The Arabic 'in shaa akhadhaha... wa in shaa kallafa' indicates a disjunctive choice.
3
Understand the legal basis
The Hanafi position is based on the pre-emptor's right being established from the sale contract. The buyer's improvements are considered a form of usurpation (ghasb) of the pre-emptor's right, so the pre-emptor can either ratify them (by paying their value) or demand their removal.
This differs from some other schools that may not allow forced removal.
4
Apply to a concrete scenario
Consider a case: A sells his house to B for 100,000. B builds an extension costing 20,000. Then A's co-owner C (pre-emptor) demands shuf'ah. C can either pay 120,000 and keep the extension, or pay only 100,000 and force B to remove the extension at B's expense.
Note that the original price remains fixed; only the improvement value is added or removed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل اذا بنى المشترى او غرس ثم قضى للشفيع بالشفعة فهو بالخيار ان شا اخذها بالثمن وقيمة البناء والغرس وان شاءكلف المشترى قلعه
Section: When the buyer builds or plants, then the pre-emptor is decreed the pre-emption, he has the option: if he wishes, he takes it with the price and the value of the building and planting, and if he wishes, he imposes on the buyer its removal.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage introduces a new section (fasl) on changes to the sold property after sale but before shuf'ah is exercised. The Hanafi ruling gives the pre-emptor a choice: (1) he may take the property by paying the original sale price plus the current value of any improvements (building or trees) made by the buyer, or (2) he may force the buyer to remove those improvements at the buyer's own expense. This option protects both parties: the buyer's investment is either compensated or removed, and the pre-emptor receives the property in its original or improved state as he chooses. The basis is that the pre-emptor's right vests at the time of sale, but subsequent changes by the buyer create a balance of interests. This is a distinctive Hanafi position that encourages fairness.

Key Terms
بناء (Bina'): Building or construction added to the property by the buyer.
غرس (Gharas): Planting (trees, plants) on the land by the buyer.
قلع (Qal'): Removal; forcing the buyer to take away his improvements at his own expense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He cannot take the land at all
D) He can take the land but must pay double the price

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives the pre-emptor a choice: take the property with improvements by paying their value, or force the buyer to remove them.

Joint Pre-emption by Muslim and Dhimmi
Ruling on joint pre-emption by Muslim and dhimmi for property sold for wine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for joint pre-emption by a Muslim and a dhimmi when the property was sold for wine, and explain the qiyas (analogy) used to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
A Muslim pre-emptor must pay the value of wine; a dhimmi may give the wine itself.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in the law of pre-emption (shuf'ah): what happens when two co-owners—one Muslim and one dhimmi—wish to exercise their right to pre-empt a property that the buyer purchased with wine. The ruling is derived through qiyas on the case of a single pre-emptor, and the reasoning hinges on the Islamic prohibition of wine for Muslims and its permissibility for dhimmis. Let us unpack the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that we have two pre-emptors: a Muslim and a dhimmi. The buyer bought a house for wine. Each pre-emptor wants to take his half-share.
The property is immovable and subject to shuf'ah.
2
State the ruling for each
The Muslim takes his half by paying half the value of the wine, not the wine itself. The dhimmi takes his half by giving half the wine (since he can lawfully possess it).
This is the same as if each were pre-empting alone.
3
Understand the qiyas (analogy)
The part (half) is analogized to the whole. The ruling for a single pre-emptor taking the entire property (paying value if Muslim, wine if dhimmi) applies equally to each share.
Illa: inability of the Muslim to give wine due to religious prohibition.
4
Consider the case of conversion
If the dhimmi becomes Muslim before or during the pre-emption, he too must pay the value, not the wine, because Islam prohibits him from taking wine and strengthens his right.
Analogy to the case where the buyer paid dates that later disappeared.
5
Apply the principle
The underlying principle: a pre-emptor must give the same thing as the buyer gave, but if that thing is unlawful for him (wine), he pays its value instead. This preserves the right without violating Islamic law.
This is a manifestation of istihsan in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة
۷۴
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
ترجمہ ۔ اور اگر اس کا شفیع مسلمان اور ذمی ہو تو مسلمان اس کے نصف کو شراب کی قیمت کے نصف کے بدلہ لے گا اور ذمی اس کے نصف کو شراب کے نصف کے بدلہ بعض کو کل پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ میں اگر ذمی مسلمان ہو گیا تو لے لے گا اس کو شراب کی قیمت کے نصف کے بدلہ اس کے عاجز ہونے کی وجہ سے شراب کا مالک بنانے سے اور اسلام کی وجہ سے اس کا حق موکد گر ہوتا ہے نہ یہ کہ باطل ہو جائے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ جبکہ خریدا ہو اس کو ایک کر کھجور کے بدلہ پھر شفیع حاضر ہوا کھجور کے منقطع ہونے کے بعد تو لے لے گا وہ اس کو کھجور کی قیمت کے بدلہ ، ایسے ہی یہ ہے۔
تشریح اگر اسی مذکورہ گھر کا شفیع مسلمان اور ذمی دونوں ہوں تو اب کیا حکم ہے تو جواب دیا کہ جیسے ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کا حکم انفراد کی صورت میں تھا ایسا ہی اب ہے۔ یعنی مسلمان اس مکان کا نصف حصہ لے گا اور بدلہ میں شراب کی قیمت کا نصف ادا کرے گا۔ کیونکہ مسلمان اپنے اسلام کی وجہ سے شراب دینے سے عاجز ہے۔ اور امی اس مکان کا نصف لے گا اور اس جیسی شراب کا نصف دے گا کیونکہ کل شفعہ لینے کی صورت میں بھی یہی حکم تھا بعض کی صورت میں بھی یہی حکم ہوگا۔ اور اگر مسلمان کا ساتھی می بھی مسلمان ہو گیا تو پھر اس کا بھی وہی حکم ہے جو مسلمان کا بیان کیا جاچکا ہے یعنی یہ بھی شراب کی قیمت کے نصف کے بدلہ اس کو لے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ شراب نہیں دے سکتا اور اسلام کی وجہ سے اس کا حق باطل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اور مضبوط ہوتا ہے اور شراب دینے کی گنجائش نہیں ۔
لہذا وہی صورت متعین ہوگی ، جو ہم نے بیان کی یعنی شراب کی قیمت کا نصف۔
فصار .. الخ سے فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مشتری نے ایک کر کھجور کے بدلہ مکان خریدا اور شفیع جس وقت سفرت آیا اس وقت کھجور بازار سے منقطع ہو گئی، یعنی گویا شفیع کھجور دینے سے عاجز ہو گیا تو پھر شفیع ان کھجوروں کی قیمت کے بدلے مکان کو شفعہ میں لے گا۔ اسی طرح یہاں ہے۔ تنبیہ گر ، یہ ایک پیا نہ ہے جو بارہ وسق کا ہوتا ہے اور ایک وسق پانچی مسن ڈھائی کلو کا ہوتا ہے تو کر کا وزن ساٹھ من نوے کلو ہوا عینی چو میں کو پھل تو نے کلو۔
And if the pre-emptor is a Muslim and a dhimmi, then the Muslim takes half of it in exchange for half the price of wine, and the dhimmi takes half in exchange for half the wine, analogizing the part to the whole. If the dhimmi becomes Muslim, he takes it in exchange for half the price of wine because he is unable to make the buyer owner of wine due to his incapacity, and because Islam strengthens his right rather than nullifying it. So it becomes like the case where the buyer bought a house for a kurr of dates, then the pre-emptor appeared after the dates had disappeared from the market – he takes it in exchange for the price of the dates. Similarly here.

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on pre-emption (shuf'ah) when the pre-emptors are a Muslim and a dhimmi jointly, and the buyer purchased the property in exchange for wine. The passage begins by stating the ruling: the Muslim takes his half of the property by paying half the value of the wine, while the dhimmi takes his half by paying half the wine itself. This is by analogy (qiyas) from the case of the whole property being taken by one pre-emptor – the ruling for each individual applies to their respective share. The commentary then explains the reasoning: the Muslim cannot take wine because it is unlawful for him, so he pays its value instead. If the dhimmi subsequently embraces Islam, he too must pay the value, because his right is strengthened by Islam and he is now unable to take wine. The passage draws an analogy to the case where the buyer bought a house for a kurr of dates, but when the pre-emptor comes, dates are no longer available; the pre-emptor then pays the price of the dates. The concluding note clarifies the weight of a kurr (60 mans or 90 kg).

Key Terms
شفیع (shafi'): The pre-emptor who has the right of shuf'ah to buy the property from the buyer.
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state who is allowed to consume wine.
شفعہ (shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption to take the property sold.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim pre-emptor must pay the value of wine when the property was sold for wine, while a dhimmi can take the wine itself; if the dhimmi converts, he too pays the value.

Pre-emptor's Options When Buyer Has Built or Planted
Ruling on pre-emptor's choice when buyer has made constructions or plantings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions (Hanafi Zahir al-Riwayah, Abu Yusuf, and Shafi'i) on the pre-emptor's options when the buyer has made improvements, and explain the practical difference.

Core Idea
The pre-emptor may force removal of the buyer's building, but Abu Yusuf disagrees — a key intra-Hanafi dispute.

When a buyer builds on land later subject to pre-emption, the law must balance the pre-emptor's right to the land as it was with the buyer's investment. Our passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the ruling from the Zahir al-Riwayah and then introduces the dissenting view of Imam Abu Yusuf, with a comparative note on Imam al-Shafi'i. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of how rights and equities interact in Hanafi property law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering scenario
The buyer has built or planted on the property before the pre-emptor's right is adjudicated. Note that the buyer acted in good faith believing the property was his.
This scenario is the basis for the entire discussion.
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah ruling
The pre-emptor has two options: (1) take the property by paying the purchase price and the value of improvements, or (2) force the buyer to remove the improvements.
This is the position of Imam Muhammad, considered the relied-upon view.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf holds that the buyer cannot be forced to remove; the pre-emptor may only take with compensation or abandon the pre-emption. His reasoning: the buyer built in good faith on his own property, so forcing removal is unjust.
This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Compare with Shafi'i's position
Imam al-Shafi'i agrees with Abu Yusuf that forced removal is not allowed, but adds a third option: the pre-emptor may remove the improvements but must pay the buyer for the loss in value.
Shafi'i introduces a compensation element absent in the Hanafi views.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Zahir al-Riwayah, the pre-emptor can obtain the land in its original state without paying for improvements if he chooses removal. Under Abu Yusuf, he must either accept the improvements or forfeit his right. Under Shafi'i, he can remove but must compensate for the loss.
This affects the pre-emptor's strategy and the buyer's exposure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل ی فصل ہے، مشفوع کے اندر عدم تغیر اصل ہے اور زیادتی اور نقصان کے ساتھ تغیر خواہ مشتری کے فعل سے ہو یا غیر کے یہ عارضی چیز ہے اسلئے اس کو علیحدہ فصل میں بیان فرمایا اور تغییر کی صورت میں کیا احکام ہیں ان کو یہاں فرمایا۔
مشتری نے مکان بنالیا یا درخت لگا لیا پھر شفیع کیلئے شفعہ کا فیصلہ ہوا تو شفیع کیلئے لینے کا طریقہ کار
قال : اذا بنى المشترى او غرس ثم قضى للشفيع بالشفعة فهو بالخيار ان شا اخذها بالثمن وقيمة البناء والغرس وان شاءكلف المشترى قلعه

كتاب الشمعة
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ ترجمہ نام قدوری نے کہا اور جبکہ مشترکی نے مکان بنالیا یا پودا لگا لیا پھر شفیع کیلئے شفعہ کا فیصلہ کر دیا گیا تو شفیع اختیار کے ساتھ ہے اگر چاہے اس زمین کوشن کے بدلہ لے لے اور تعمیر اور پودے کی قیمت کے بدلہ اور اگر چاہے مشتری کو اس کے اکھاڑنے کا مکلف بنائے۔ تشریح مشتری نے مکان خرید کر اس میں تعمیر بنالی یا باغ لگا لیا پھر شفیع کیلئے قاضی نے شفعہ کا فیصلہ کر دیا تو ظاہر الروایہ میں اب شفیع کے دو حکم ہیں۔
ا۔ اگر وہ چاہے تو اس زمین کا شمن اور تعمیر و پودے کی قیمت دے کر اس کو لے لے۔
۲۔ اور اگر چاہے تو مشتری سے کہہ دے کہ اپنی تعمیر و پودوں کو اکھاڑ کر لے جا۔ امام ابو یوسف کا نقطہ نظر
وعن ابى يوسف انه لا يكلف القلع ويخير بين ان ياخذ بالثمن وقيمة البنا والغرس وبين ان يترك و به قال الشافعي الا ان عنده له ان يقلع ويعطى قيمة البناء
ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ مشتری کو اکھاڑنے کا مکلف نہیں بنایا جائے گا اور اس کو شفیک) اختیار دیا جائے گا۔ اس کے درمیان کہ ثمن اور تعمیر پودے کی قیمت کے بدلے لے لے اور اس کے درمیان کہ چھوڑ دے اور یہی الشافعی نے فرمایا مگر ان کے نزدیک شفیع کو اختیار ہے کہ اکھاڑ دے اور تعمیر کے نقصان کی قیمت ادا کر دئے۔
تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کا قول نقل کیا گیا ہے کہ مشتری کو اکھاڑنے کی تکلیف نہ دی جائے بلکہ شفیع کو صرف دو اختیار ملیں گے۔ ا۔ تعمیر وغرس کی قیمت دے اور زمین کا شمن دے اور مشفوع کو لے لے۔
۲۔ شفعہ کو ہی چھوڑ دے۔
پھر فرماتے ہیں کہ امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ مگر انکے اور امام ابو یوسف کے قول میں کچھ فرق ہے۔ یعنی امام ابو یوسف کے دو قول ہیں اور امام شافعی کے تین ، شمن اور قیمت تعمیر ادا کر کے زمین کو لے لے۔
۲۔ شفعہ ہی چھوڑ دے۔
۳۔ مشتری کو اپنی تعمیر توڑنے کی تکلیف دے اور ٹوٹنے کی وجہ سے اس کی مالیت میں جو کمی آئی ہے اس نقصان کو ادا کر دے، الا ان عنده له ان يقلع ويعطى قيمة البناء سے مصنف نے یہی فرمایا ہے۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل
لابي يوسف انه محق في البنا لانه بناه على ان الدار ملكه والتكليف بالقلع من احكام العدو وان وصار كالموهوب له والمشترى شر و فاسدا كذا ازرع المشترى فانه لا يكلف القلع ترجمہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشتری تعمیر کرنے میں حق پر ہے. اسلئے کہ اس نے مکان اسلئے بنایا کہ دار اس کی ملکیت ہے اور
Chapter: This chapter is about changes to the property subject to pre-emption. The original state is absence of change, but increase or decrease due to the buyer's or others' actions is accidental. The ruling: When the buyer has built or planted, and then the pre-emptor is awarded pre-emption, he has the option: if he wishes, he takes the property with the price and the value of the building and planting; if he wishes, he forces the buyer to remove them. From Abu Yusuf: The buyer is not forced to remove; the pre-emptor is given the choice between taking with the price and value, or leaving it. Al-Shafi'i said likewise, except that in his view the pre-emptor may remove and give the value of the building. The proof of Abu Yusuf: The buyer was justified in building because he built on the basis that the house was his property, and forcing removal is a penalty, so it is like a gift.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where the buyer (mushtari) has made improvements (building or planting) on the property before the pre-emptor's right is adjudicated. The passage first states the ruling from the original text (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): the pre-emptor has two options: either take the property by paying the purchase price plus the value of the improvements, or require the buyer to remove them. This is the position of the Zahir al-Riwayah (Imam Muhammad). The commentary then presents the view of Imam Abu Yusuf, who does not allow forcing the buyer to remove; instead, the pre-emptor may only take the property with compensation or abandon the pre-emption entirely. Imam al-Shafi'i is reported to have a similar view but adds a third option: the pre-emptor may remove the improvements and pay the reduction in value. The passage includes Abu Yusuf's reasoning: the buyer built in good faith believing the property was his, so forcing removal would be punitive. The discussion highlights a key intra-Hanafi dispute and a cross-madhhab comparison.

Key Terms
قلع (qal'): Removal or demolition of the buyer's construction or uprooting of plants.
غرس (ghars): Planting trees or vegetation on the property.
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption to take the property from the buyer at the sale price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, what options does the pre-emptor have if the buyer has built on the property?
A) Only take the property with compensation for the building
B) Only force the buyer to remove the building
C) Either take the property with compensation or force removal
D) Must abandon the pre-emption

Key Takeaway
Under the Hanafi Zahir al-Riwayah, the pre-emptor may force the buyer to remove improvements without compensation, but this is contested by Abu Yusuf and differs from the Shafi'i position.

Options of the Pre-emptor When Buyer Has Made Improvements
States the two options for the pre-emptor with improvements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options of the pre-emptor under Zahir al-Riwayah when the buyer has built or planted, and apply the ruling to a new scenario.

Core Idea
The pre-emptor can either take improvements with compensation or compel their removal.

When a buyer has made improvements—like building a house or planting trees—on property subject to pre-emption, the pre-emptor (shafi') is not forced to accept the improvements at face value. Instead, the Hanafi school, in its Zahir al-Riwayah, gives him a clear choice. This passage from Al-Hidayah lays out those two options, balancing the rights of both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with the pre-emptor's options after a successful claim of shuf'ah. The act is exercising pre-emption over property that has been improved by the buyer.
The ruling is that the pre-emptor has two permissible choices.
2
State the First Option
The pre-emptor may take the land along with the building or trees by paying the buyer their value (in addition to the land price).
This option requires fair compensation for improvements.
3
State the Second Option
Alternatively, the pre-emptor may demand that the buyer remove the building or trees at the buyer's own expense.
The pre-emptor does not pay for removal costs or depreciation.
4
Note the Authoritative Basis
Both options come from Zahir al-Riwayah, the core transmitted texts of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. This is the relied-upon position in the school.
Other views (Abu Yusuf, Shafi'i) differ and will be treated separately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة
اشرف الهداية شرح اردو هداية جلد ۱۳ ترجمہ نام قدوری نے کہا اور جبکہ مشتری نے مکان بنالیا یا پودا لگا لیا پھر شفیع کیلئے شفعہ کا فیصلہ کر دیا گیا تو شفیع اختیار کے ساتھ ہے اگر چاہے اس زمین کو ثمن کے بدلہ لے لے اور تعمیر اور پودے کی قیمت کے بدلہ اور اگر چاہے مشتری کو اس کے اکھاڑنے کا مکلف بنائے۔ تشریح مشتری نے مکان خرید کر اس میں تعمیر بنالی یا باغ لگا لیا پھر شفیع کیلئے قاضی نے شفعہ کا فیصلہ کر دیا تو ظاہر الروایہ میں اب شفیع کے دو حکم ہیں۔ ا۔ اگر وہ چاہے تو اس زمین کا ثمن اور تعمیر و پودے کی قیمت دے کر اس کو لے لے۔ ۲۔ اور اگر چاہے تو مشتری سے کہہ دے کہ اپنی تعمیر و پودوں کو اکھاڑ کر لے جا۔
Book of Pre-emption. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya volume 13. Translation: Al-Quduri said: When the buyer has built a house or planted a tree, then the pre-emptor has been adjudicated in his favor, then the pre-emptor has an option: if he wishes, he may take the land in exchange for its price and the value of the building and plantation, and if he wishes, he may compel the buyer to remove them. Explanation: The buyer purchased the land and built upon it or planted a garden, then the judge decided the pre-emption in favor of the pre-emptor. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, the pre-emptor now has two rulings: 1. If he wishes, he may give the price of the land and the value of the building and plantation and take them. 2. If he wishes, he may tell the buyer to remove his building and plantations and take them away.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) from the Hanafi school regarding the pre-emptor's options when the buyer has made improvements (construction or planting) after purchasing the property. The key point is that the pre-emptor has two equally valid choices: he may either compensate the buyer for the improvements along with the land price and retain them, or he may demand that the buyer remove them at his own expense. Note that the pre-emptor is not required to pay for any depreciation caused by removal; that loss is borne by the buyer. This ruling is from the core texts of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): Pre-emption; the right of a co-owner or neighbour to purchase property sold to an outsider under certain conditions.
شفيع (shafi'): The pre-emptor; the person entitled to exercise shuf'ah.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The manifest transmission; the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that form the authoritative basis of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what options does the pre-emptor have when the buyer has built on the land?
A) Take the land with improvements paying their value, or compel removal.
B) Only take the land without improvements.
C) Only compel removal without payment.
D) Forfeit the pre-emption right.

Key Takeaway
Under Zahir al-Riwayah, the pre-emptor has a choice: either compensate the buyer for improvements and keep them, or have the buyer remove them at his own cost.

Pre-emptor's Options with Improvements: Abu Yusuf's Two-Option Rule
Presents Abu Yusuf's opinion and his proofs that the pre-emptor cannot compel removal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Yusuf's two-option rule for the pre-emptor when the buyer has made improvements, and evaluate his qiyas-based argument against the Zahir al-Riwayah position.

Core Idea
A good-faith improver cannot be forced to demolish; the pre-emptor must either pay or leave.

When a buyer builds or plants on purchased land, then a pre-emptor appears, what options does the pre-emptor have? Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the buyer, having acted in good faith on what he believed was his property, cannot be compelled to remove his improvements. The pre-emptor is limited to two choices: take the property with compensation for improvements, or abandon pre-emption. This view differs from the relied-upon Hanafi position. We will unpack his proofs and understand the legal reasoning behind this intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the ikhtilaf
Identify the exact point of dispute: does the pre-emptor have the right to compel the buyer to demolish improvements made in good faith?
This is an intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Yusuf and the Zahir al-Riwayah (Abu Hanifa).
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's position
Read the passage to determine Abu Yusuf's ruling: the pre-emptor has only two options (take with payment or leave), not three. Understand the rationale: the buyer is justified (muhaqq) in building.
The buyer's good faith is central.
3
Examine the qiyas proofs
Abu Yusuf draws three analogies: donee building on gifted land, buyer in a fasid sale building, and buyer planting crops. In each, the improver is not forced to remove. Identify the common illa: the improver acted within his apparent ownership.
This is qiyas, not direct text.
4
Apply the lesser harm principle
Abu Yusuf concludes that the law chooses the lesser of two harms: requiring the pre-emptor to pay is less harmful than forcing demolition. Understand how this principle guides the ruling.
This is a form of istihsan via daf' al-darar.
5
Compare with the mufta bihi position
Note that the relied-upon (Zahir al-Riwayah) position gives the pre-emptor an extra option: compel removal without compensation. Identify why Abu Yusuf's view is not mufta bihi.
Tarjih authority: Al-Marghinani prefers Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن ابى يوسف انه لا يكلف القلع ويخير بين ان ياخذ بالثمن وقيمة البنا والغرس وبين ان يترك و به قال الشافعي الا ان عنده له ان يقلع ويعطى قيمة البناء ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ مشتری کو اکھاڑنے کا مکلف نہیں بنایا جائے گا اور اس کو شفیع کو اختیار دیا جائے گا۔ اس کے درمیان کہ ثمن اور تعمیر پودے کی قیمت کے بدلے لے لے اور اس کے درمیان کہ چھوڑ دے اور یہی الشافعی نے فرمایا مگر ان کے نزدیک شفیع کو اختیار ہے کہ اکھاڑ دے اور تعمیر کے نقصان کی قیمت ادا کر دئے۔ تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کا قول نقل کیا گیا ہے کہ مشتری کو اکھاڑنے کی تکلیف نہ دی جائے بلکہ شفیع کو صرف دو اختیار ملیں گے۔ ا۔ تعمیر وغرس کی قیمت دے اور زمین کا شمن دے اور مشفوع کو لے لے۔ ۲۔ شفعہ کو ہی چھوڑ دے۔ پھر فرماتے ہیں کہ امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ مگر انکے اور امام ابو یوسف کے قول میں کچھ فرق ہے۔ یعنی امام ابو یوسف کے دو قول ہیں اور امام شافعی کے تین ، شمن اور قیمت تعمیر ادا کر کے زمین کو لے لے۔ ۲۔ شفعہ ہی چھوڑ دے۔ ۳۔ مشتری کو اپنی تعمیر توڑنے کی تکلیف دے اور ٹوٹنے کی وجہ سے اس کی مالیت میں جو کمی آئی ہے اس نقصان کو ادا کر دے، الا ان عنده له ان يقلع ويعطى قيمة البناء سے مصنف نے یہی فرمایا ہے۔
لابي يوسف انه محق في البنا لانه بناه على ان الدار ملكه والتكليف بالقلع من احكام العدو وان وصار كالموهوب له والمشترى شر و فاسدا كذا ازرع المشترى فانه لا يكلف القلع ترجمہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشتری تعمیر کرنے میں حق پر ہے. اسلئے کہ اس نے مکان اسلئے بنایا کہ دار اس کی ملکیت ہے اور اکھاڑنے کی تکلیف دینا ظلم کے احکام میں سے ہے اور ایسا ہو گیا جیسے موہوب لہ اور جیسے وہ چیز جس کو شراء فاسد کے ساتھ خریدا گیا ہو اور جسے جبکہ مشتری نے کھیتی بودی ہو تو ان میں سے کوئی اکھاڑنے کا مکلف نہیں بنایا جائے گا۔ تشریح امام ابو یوسف دلیل پیش کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ مشتری نے ظلما تعمیر نہیں کی بلکہ اپنی ملک میں کی تو مشتری اس تصرف میں حق پر ہے پھر اس کو اکھاڑنے کا حکم دینا ظلم وزیادتی ہے۔ اس کے بعام بو یوسف نے اس پر تین شواہد پیش کیئے :- ا۔ اگر واہب نے کوئی زمین کسی کو ہبہ کردی اور موہوب لڑ نے (جس کو ہبہ کی گئی ہے ) اس پر مکان تعمیر کر دیا اب واہب چاہتا ہے کہ اس کا مکان اکھٹروادوں اور زمین کو واپس لے لوں تو واہب کو یہ اختیار نہیں ، ایسے ہی یہاں بھی ہوگا۔ ۲۔ مشتری نے کوئی زمین شراء فاسد کے ساتھ خریدی اور پھر اس پر مکان تعمیر کر دیا۔ اب بائع چاہتا ہے کہ مکان اکھٹر وا کر زمین واپس لے لوں تو بائع کو اس کا حق نہیں ہے۔ ایسے ہی یہاں شفیع کو کھڑوانے کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ ۔ مشتری نے زمین خریدی اور اس میں کھیتی کی فصل کھڑی ہوئی ہے کہ اس زمین کے بارے میں قاضی نے شفیع کے حق میں فیصلہ کر دیا اب شفیع چاہتا ہے کہ اسکی فصل کٹوا کر زمین پر قبضہ کر لوں تو شفیع کو یہ حق نہ ہوگا۔ ایسے ہی تعمیر وغیرہ اکھڑوانے کا بھی حق نہ ہوگا۔
وهذا لان فى ايجاب الاخذ بالقيمة دفع اعلى الضررين بتحمل الأدنى فيصـار اليـه ترجمہ اور یہ اسلئے کہ قیمت کے بدلے لینے کو واجب کرنے میں دوسروں میں سے اعلیٰ کو دور کرتا ہے۔ ادنی کا مکمل کر کے تو اسی کی جانب رجوع کیا جائے گا۔
And from Abu Yusuf that he does not compel removal and gives the shafi' a choice between taking with the price and value of the building and planting, and between leaving. And Imam al-Shafi'i said the same, except that according to him he may compel removal and give the value of the building... Explanation: This is the statement of Imam Abu Yusuf: the buyer is not compelled to remove; rather the shafi' will have only two options: 1) give the price of the land and the value of the building/planting and take the property, or 2) leave the pre-emption. Then he says that Imam al-Shafi'i also holds this view, but there is a difference between his and Abu Yusuf's statement: Abu Yusuf has two options, while Shafi'i has three: 1) take the land by paying the price and value of building, 2) leave the pre-emption altogether, 3) compel the buyer to demolish his building and pay the depreciation in value...
For Abu Yusuf: He is justified in building because he built on the assumption that the house was his property; requiring demolition is from the rulings of oppression. And it becomes like the donee and the buyer in a defective sale, and likewise the buyer who plants crops is not compelled to remove.
And this is because in requiring taking with value, the higher of two harms is repelled by enduring the lower, so recourse is to that.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage presents the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf (d. 182 AH), a chief disciple of Abu Hanifa, who disagrees with the Zahir al-Riwayah position. Abu Yusuf argues that the buyer, having built in good faith on what he believed was his own property, should not be forced to demolish his construction. Instead, the pre-emptor has only two choices: either take the land and pay for the improvements, or abandon his right of pre-emption entirely. Abu Yusuf supports this with three analogies: (1) a donee who builds on gifted land cannot be compelled to remove if the donor reclaims; (2) a buyer in a defective sale (shira' fاسد) who builds; and (3) a buyer who plants crops. In each case, the improver is not forced to remove. He further invokes the principle of choosing the lesser harm: forcing the buyer to demolish causes severe harm, whereas obligating the pre-emptor to pay for improvements is a lighter harm. Hence, the law should adopt the latter. Note that Imam al-Shafi'i shares Abu Yusuf's view but adds a third option: the pre-emptor may compel removal while compensating the buyer for depreciation.

Key Terms
قلع (qal'): Removal or demolition of a building or uprooting of plants.
موهوب له (mawhub lahu): The donee; the recipient of a gift (hiba).
شراء فاسد (shira' fاسد): A defective sale; a sale that is voidable due to a missing condition but may be validated by consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, how many options does the pre-emptor have when the buyer has made improvements?
A) Two: take with compensation or leave.
B) Three: take, leave, or compel removal with compensation.
C) One: only compel removal without compensation.
D) Four: including negotiation.

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf's view on pre-emptor's options illustrates the use of qiyas and the principle of choosing the lesser harm, but the mufta bihi position follows the Zahir al-Riwayah allowing compulsion without compensation.

Proof of Zahir al-Riwayah: Pre-emptor Can Compel Removal
Provides the analogical proof for the relied-upon Hanafi position allowing compulsory removal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that a pre-emptor can compel removal of improvements and explain the analogical proof (qiyas) on which it is based.

Core Idea
A pre-emptor's strong right (haqq mu'takad) overrides the buyer's ownership, allowing him to demand removal of improvements.

The Zahir al-Riwayah position gives the pre-emptor a powerful tool: he can force the buyer to tear down any building or improvement made on the land before his right was settled. This ruling is not arbitrary; it is derived through a precise legal analogy (qiyas) to the case of a mortgagor building on mortgaged property. In this lesson, we will break down that analogy, examine the underlying logic, and see how it differs from other views within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling being proved
State clearly what Zahir al-Riwayah holds: the pre-emptor can compel the buyer to remove improvements at his own expense.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the asl (original case) of the analogy
The asl is the mortgagor (rahin) who builds on mortgaged property (marhun) without permission. The mortgagee can compel removal.
The mortgagee's right (haqq al-rahn) is a strong right similar to shuf'ah.
3
Extract the illa (effective cause)
The illa is: a person builds on property subject to another's strong right (haqq mu'takad) without authorization from the right-holder.
The right is 'strong' because it pre-dates the builder's ownership and can even annul transfers.
4
Apply to the far' (new case)
The buyer's situation matches the illa: he built on land that was already subject to the pre-emptor's haqq mu'takad, without his permission.
Hence the same ruling applies: the pre-emptor can compel removal.
5
Consider the objection and response
Abu Yusuf objects that the buyer owns the property and should not be compelled. The Hanafi response: the pre-emptor's right is stronger than the buyer's ownership, so it can override.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجه ظاهر الرواية انه بنى فى محل تعلق به حق متاكد للغير من غير تسليط من جهة من له الحق فينقص كالراهن اذابنى فى المرهون وهذا لان حقه اقوى من حق المشترى لانه يتقدم عليه ولهذا ينقض بيعه وهبته وغيره من تصرفاته ترجمہ اور ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشتری نے ایسے محل میں مکان تعمیر کیا کہ جس کے ساتھ غیر کا مضبوط حق وابستہ ہے۔ مسن له
And the proof of Zahir al-Riwayah is that he built in a place to which a strong right of another is attached, without authorization from the one having the right, so he is deficient, like the mortgagor when he builds on the mortgaged property. And this is because his right is stronger than the right of the buyer, because it precedes him, and for this reason his sale, gift, and other dispositions are annulled.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage provides the formal proof for the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) that the pre-emptor can compel the buyer to remove his improvements. The key argument is analogical (qiyas): the buyer built on property that was already subject to the pre-emptor's strong right (haqq mu'takad). This right is so powerful that it can invalidate the buyer's sale and other transactions. Therefore, the buyer's position is analogous to that of a mortgagor who builds on mortgaged property without the mortgagee's permission. Just as the mortgagee can demand removal of such construction, so too can the pre-emptor. Note that the pre-emptor's right predates and overrides the buyer's ownership, so the buyer's act of building is akin to trespass on another's right.

Key Terms
حق متاكد (haqq mu'takad): A strong or established right; in this context, the pre-emptor's right that is attached to the property before the buyer's ownership.
راهن (rahin): Mortgagor; the person who pledges property as security for a debt.
مرهون (marhun): The mortgaged property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
To what situation does Zahir al-Riwayah analogize the buyer who builds on pre-empted land?
A) A mortgagor building on mortgaged property.
B) A donee building on gifted land.
C) A buyer in a defective sale building.
D) A tenant building on leased land.

Key Takeaway
The pre-emptor's right (haqq mu'takad) is so strong that it can invalidate the buyer's ownership and justify compelling removal of improvements.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Building by Buyer Before Pre-emption: Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the fate of buyer's improvements in pre-emption.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) and the opposing view (Abu Yusuf) on whether the pre-emptor can force the buyer to demolish improvements, and explain the legal reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
The pre-emptor's prior right trumps the buyer's building unless the buyer had authorization.

In Hanafi fiqh, the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) gives the pre-emptor a claim to a property sold to a third party. But what happens when the buyer makes improvements before the pre-emptor exercises his right? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf. Abu Hanifa holds that the pre-emptor can force demolition without compensation; Abu Yusuf argues the pre-emptor must compensate for improvements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The dispute is about whether the pre-emptor (shafi‘) can force the buyer (mushtari) to demolish buildings/plants on the land before taking possession.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and analogies
Abu Yusuf argues the buyer built on his own property, so forcing demolition is oppressive. He gives three analogies: gift, invalid sale, and crops.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position (Zahir al-Riwayah)
Abu Hanifa holds that the buyer built without authorization from the pre-emptor, whose right is stronger, so the building must be demolished, like a pledgor building in pledged property.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf's analogies
The cases of gift and invalid sale involve authorization from the donor/seller, whereas the pre-emptor never authorized the buyer. Also, the right of revocation in those cases is weak and does not survive construction, but the pre-emptor's right remains.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical consequence: According to Abu Yusuf, the pre-emptor must pay the value of improvements; according to Abu Hanifa, he takes the land free and can force removal. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view (Zahir al-Riwayah).

اکھاڑنے کی تکلیف دینا ظلم کے احکام میں سے ہے اور ایسا ہو گیا جیسے موہوب لہ اور جیسے وہ چیز جس کو شراء فاسد کے ساتھ خریدا گیا ہو اور جسے جبکہ مشتری نے کھیتی بودی ہو تو ان میں سے کوئی اکھاڑنے کا مکلف نہیں بنایا جائے گا۔
