Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct rulings from the matn. First, if the right of faskh (rescission) in a fasid sale becomes impossible (e.g., the buyer resells the property to a third party), then the impediment to shuf'ah is removed, and the shafi' (original co-owner or neighbor) may claim shuf'ah. Second, a new ruling: In a fasid sale where the sold property (mabi') remains in the seller's possession, and an adjacent house is sold, the seller has the right of shuf'ah because he still owns that property. However, if the seller has already handed the mabi' over to the buyer, then the buyer is the owner and becomes the shafi'. The passage then details the effect of timing relative to the shuf'ah judgment: If the seller hands over the mabi' to the buyer before the judge's ruling on his shuf'ah claim, his shuf'ah becomes void because he no longer owns the property that was the basis of his claim. But if he hands it over after the judgment, his shuf'ah remains valid because continuity of ownership after judgment is not a condition; the shuf'ah right is confirmed at the time of judgment. Conversely, if the seller recovers the mabi' from the buyer before judgment, his shuf'ah becomes void because his ownership was severed at the time of recovery. If he recovers after judgment, his shuf'ah remains. The commentary also draws an analogy: if a person claiming shuf'ah sells his own property before judgment, his shuf'ah claim becomes void, similar to the seller handing over the mabi' before judgment. The passage is a commentary on the matn of al-Hidayah, explaining these rulings with examples.

Key Terms
حق الفسخ (haqq al-faskh): The right to rescind a contract, here specifically the right to annul a fasid sale.
مانع (mani'): The impediment that prevents shuf'ah from being established, in this context the possibility of faskh.
حکم بالشفعة (hukm bi al-shuf'ah): The judge's decision granting the right of preemption to the claimant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The shuf'ah claim remains valid because ownership is not required.
B) The shuf'ah claim becomes void because the buyer no longer owns the property that formed the basis of the claim.
C) The shuf'ah claim becomes void only if the seller explicitly revokes it.
D) The shuf'ah claim remains valid and transfers to the seller.

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah in a fasid sale is established when the right of faskh is removed, and the shafi''s ownership at the time of judgment is crucial.

Effect of Returning Fasid Sale on Pre-emption
Ruling with proof on shuf'ah and fasid sale rescission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing the timing of rescission of a fasid sale to determine whether the pre-emptor's right is preserved or lost.

Core Idea
Pre-emption right is lost if the triggering property is returned before judgment, but stands if returned after.

This passage addresses a critical nuance in the law of pre-emption (shuf'ah): when the property that triggered the pre-emption right is sold in a fasid (defective) sale, and that sale is later rescinded by legal ruling, does the pre-emptor keep his right? The Hanafi school resolves this by looking at the timing of the rescission relative to the judge's decree. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying shuf'ah in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A fasid sale has occurred: the seller delivered the property to the buyer, and another house was sold to a pre-emptor. The original seller later recovers his property due to the defect.
The fasid sale is rescinded by legal ruling, not by mutual agreement.
2
Apply the timing distinction
Determine whether the rescission occurred before or after the judge's decree granting pre-emption to the buyer.
Before judgment: pre-emption is lost. After judgment: pre-emption is upheld.
3
State the legal basis
The ruling rests on the principle that once pre-emption is decreed, ownership of the pre-empted property does not depend on continued ownership of the triggering property.
The proof is analogical (qiyas) to the seller's own pre-emption case mentioned earlier.

Source Text

بائع نے مبیع کو مشتری کے حوالہ کیا ہو تو اب جس مکان کو بائع شفعہ میں لے چکا ہے وہ اس کا ہے اس میں شفعہ باطل نہ ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ یہ اصول مقر ر ہے کہ جس گھر کی وجہ سے شفعہ لیا ہے قاضی کے فیصلہ کے بعد بھی اس میں ملکیت کا برابر باقی رہنا بالاتفاق شرط نہیں ہے۔ وان استردها.. الخ صبیح بیع فاسد میں مشتری کے قبضہ میں جاچکا اور اس کے برابر میں جو مکان فروخت ہوا۔ مشتری نے اس میں شفعہ کا دعوی کیا اور اسی حالت میں بیج کے اندر فساد کی وجہ سے بحکم شرعی بائع نے مبیع کو مشتری سے واپس لے لیا تو اب مشتری کو شفعہ ملے گا یا نہیں؟ تو جواب دیا کہ اگر بائع نے مشتری کے حق میں شفعہ کا حکم ہونے سے پہلے واپس لے لیا تو مشتری کو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا اور اگر حکم شفعہ ہو جانے کے بعد واپس لیا ہو تو واپسی درست ہے اور جو مکان مشتری شفعہ میں لے چکا ہے وہ اس کا ہے۔ دلیل وہی ہے جو بائع کے بیان میں گزر چکی ہے۔
If the seller has delivered the sold item to the buyer, then the house that the seller has taken by pre-emption is his; pre-emption is not invalidated in it. Because it is an established principle that for the house on account of which pre-emption was taken, it is not a condition by consensus that equal ownership remains even after the judge's decision. 'And if he takes it back...' etc. In a fasid sale that has come into the buyer's possession, and in exchange a house was sold, the buyer claimed pre-emption in it, and in that state, due to the defect in the sale, by legal ruling the seller took back the sold item from the buyer, then will the buyer get pre-emption or not? The answer was: if the seller took it back before the pre-emption judgment in favor of the buyer, then the buyer will not get pre-emption; and if he took it back after the pre-emption judgment, then the return is valid and the house that the buyer took by pre-emption is his. The proof is the same as already mentioned in the statement of the seller.

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of rescinding a fasid (defective) sale on the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah). It is a ruling statement with proof. The text first establishes a general principle: once a pre-emptor takes a property by pre-emption, it becomes his and is not invalidated even if the seller recovers the original property. Then it presents a specific case: a fasid sale where the buyer took possession, and the seller later recovers the property by legal ruling due to the defect. The ruling distinguishes timing: if the recovery occurs before the judge's decree granting pre-emption to the buyer (who is now the original seller in the second sale?), the pre-emptor loses his right; if after, the pre-emption stands. The proof is a previously established principle that ownership of the pre-empted property does not depend on continued ownership of the triggering property.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption in property sales, allowing a co-owner or neighbor to purchase the property instead of the outsider.
بیع فاسد (bay' fasid): A sale that is defective in essence but valid in form, requiring a condition (like delivery) to be corrected; here, the sale is rescinded by legal order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The timing of rescission of a fasid sale relative to the shuf'ah judgment determines whether the pre-emptor's right is preserved or lost.

No Pre-emption in Partition (Qismah) Among Co-Sharers
Ruling that partition does not give pre-emption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pre-emption in partition of joint property and explain the legal reasoning that distinguishes partition from sale.

Core Idea
Partition is separation, not sale — pre-emption only applies to absolute exchanges.

In this lesson, we examine a concise ruling from al-Quduri's matn: when co-sharers divide a jointly owned property, a neighbor (or non-sharer) does not acquire a right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) through that division. The commentary unpacks the reasoning: partition is a mere separation of shares (ifraz), not a transfer of ownership by exchange. This distinction is crucial because the institution of shuf'ah is legislated only for sales, not for partitions or gifts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is partition of joint property among co-sharers. The ruling is that shuf'ah does not arise for a neighbor.
2
Locate the dalil
The text states the proof: partition contains the meaning of ifraz (separation), and pre-emption is only legislated for absolute exchange (mubadalah mutlaqah). Additionally, partition allows compulsion (jabr) unlike sale.
The proof is from the general principle restricting shuf'ah to sales.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key is that shuf'ah is restricted to sales by the phrase 'mubadalah mutlaqah'. Partition is not a sale because it is a separation without exchange. The presence of jabr in partition further confirms it is not a sale.
The illa (effective cause) for shuf'ah is the presence of an absolute exchange; partition lacks this illa.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
This ruling is the standard Hanafi position; some other schools may allow shuf'ah in certain partitions, but the Hanafi school strictly limits it to sales.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih, but the Hanafi position is clear.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is as stated: no shuf'ah in partition. The authority is from Zahir al-Riwayah via Quduri and al-Hidayah.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرکاء نے زمین تقسیم کی تو شفکا حق نہیں ملے گا
قال واذا اقتسم الشركاء العقار فلا شفعة لجارهم بالقسمة لان القسمة فيها معنى الافراز ولهذا يجرى فيه الجبر والشفعة ما شرعت إلا فى المبادلة المطلقة.
ترجمہ اور جبکہ شرکاء نے زمین کا بٹوارہ کیا تو بنوارہ کی وجہ سے ان کے پڑوسی کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ قسمت اس میں افراز کے معنی ہیں ( الگ الگ کرنا ) اور اسی وجہ سے اس میں جبر جاری ہوتا ہے اور شفعہ مشروع نہیں ہوا مگر مبادلہ مطلقہ میں۔
تشریح شرکاء نے اپنی زمین کا بٹوارہ کیا تو ظاہر ہے کہ یہ بیچ نہیں ہے اور مبادلہ کالی نہیں ہے بلکہ اپنے حصوں کو بانٹنا اور جدا جدا کرنا ہے جس کو افراز کہا گیا ہے۔ لہذا اگر کوئی پڑوسی بوقت بٹوارہ شفعہ کا دعوی کرے تو اس کو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ کیونکہ شرط شفعہ (بیع ) نہیں پائی گئی اور قسمت میں زمین و آسمان کا فرق ہے۔ بیع کے اندر جبر جائز نہیں بلکہ تراضی شرط ہے اور قسمت کے اندر جبر جائز ہے یعنی اگر شریکوں میں سے کوئی قسمت کا مطالبہ کرے اور دوسرا شریک انکار کرے تو منکر پر جبر کیا جائے گا اور اس کو ہوارہ پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔
When co-sharers divide land, their neighbor does not get pre-emption due to partition, because partition has the meaning of separation (ifraz), and therefore compulsion applies in it, and pre-emption is only legislated in absolute exchange. Translation: And when co-sharers divided land, then due to the division, their neighbor does not have pre-emption, because partition has the meaning of separation (making distinct), and for this reason compulsion applies in it, and pre-emption was not legislated except in absolute exchange. Explanation: Co-sharers divided their land – clearly this is not a sale, and it is not an exchange; rather it is distributing and separating their shares, which is called ifraz. Therefore if a neighbor claims pre-emption at the time of partition, he will not get pre-emption, because the condition of pre-emption (sale) is not present, and there is a great difference between partition and sale. In sale, compulsion is not allowed; mutual consent is a condition; but in partition, compulsion is allowed: i.e., if one co-sharer demands partition and another refuses, the refuser can be compelled and forced to divide.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof, establishing that partition (qismah) of jointly owned property among co-sharers does not give rise to a right of pre-emption for a neighbor (or non-co-sharer). The text quotes the original matn: Imam Quduri's statement. The proof is based on two points: (1) partition is a form of ifraz (separation of shares), not an exchange (mubadalah); (2) pre-emption is only legislated for absolute exchanges (mubadalah mutlaqah), i.e., sales. The commentary elaborates that partition involves compulsion (jabr) – a co-sharer can be forced to divide, whereas sale requires mutual consent. This distinction shows partition is not a sale, so the condition for shuf'ah (a valid sale) is absent. Hence, no pre-emption.

Key Terms
قسمت (qismah): Partition of joint property among co-owners, separating shares.
افراز (ifraz): Making distinct; separating shares without exchange.
مبادلہ مطلقہ (mubadalah mutlaqah): Absolute exchange, i.e., a sale where property is exchanged for consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because partition is a type of gift.
B) Because partition is an exchange of shares.
C) Because partition is separation, not a sale, and pre-emption only applies to sales.
D) Because the neighbor has no right in joint property.

Key Takeaway
Partition is not a sale; pre-emption is reserved for absolute exchanges only.

Waiving Pre‑emption: No Revival Upon Buyer's Return
Ruling with logical proof on shuf'ah after waiver and return

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shuf'ah after a pre-emptor's waiver and subsequent return of the property by the buyer via khiyar, and explain why it does not revive.

Core Idea
A rescission (faskh) is not a new sale; shuf'ah only arises from a new contract (insha’ al-‘aqd).

What happens when a pre-emptor initially walks away from his right, but then the buyer returns the property to the seller through a legal option? Does shuf'ah come back? This lesson unpacks a precise rule from the Hanafi school: once the pre-emptor waives, a subsequent return—even by court order for a defect—does not create a new opportunity. The key legal distinction is between a rescission (which reverts ownership to the original seller) and a fresh sale (which would trigger shuf'ah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial transaction and waiver
The buyer (mushtari) purchases a property. A pre-emptor (shafi‘) has a right to take it, but he explicitly waives that right. At this point, shuf'ah is extinguished.
Waiver is a definitive act—it does not leave a pending right.
2
Determine the nature of the buyer's return
Later, the buyer returns the property to the seller due to one of three khiyars: option of inspection, option of condition, or a hidden defect. The return must be validated by a judge's decree (qada).
The text explicitly mentions 'بقضاء قاض' (by a judge's decree) for defect cases, but implies the same for all three.
3
Classify the legal effect of the return
The return is a complete rescission (faskh min kull wajh) of the original sale. Ownership returns to the seller as if the sale never occurred. It is not a new transfer of ownership.
Faskh differs from iqalah (mutual rescission) in that it is unilateral and based on a recognized right.
4
Apply the rule for shuf'ah
Shuf'ah is only established upon the initiation of a new contract (insha’ al-‘aqd) that transfers ownership to a new party. Since the return is a rescission, there is no new contract. Therefore, the pre-emptor's right does not revive.
The Hanafi principle is clear: shuf'ah arises at the moment of sale, not at the moment of rescission.
5
Confirm irrelevance of possession
The same ruling applies whether the buyer had taken possession (qabd) of the property at the time of return or not. Possession does not change the classification of the return as faskh.
This removes a potential false distinction that students might assume.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شفیع شفعہ چھوڑ دے پھر مشتری نے خیار رویت یا خیار شرط یا خیار عیب کی وجہ سے رد کیا تو شفعہ کا پھر حق نہیں ملے گا
قال واذا اشترى دارا فسلم الشفيع الشفعة ثم ردها المشترى بخيار رؤية او شرط او بعيب بقضاء قاض فلا شفعة للشفيع لانه فسخ من كل وجه فعاد الى قديم ملكه والشفعهم إنشاء العقد ولا فرق في هذا بين القبض وعدمه
ترجمہ امام قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب مشتری نے گھر خریدا پس شفیع نے شفعہ سے دست برداری دے دی ۔ پھر مشتری نے اس گھر کو خیا روایت یا خیار شرط یا عیب کی وجہ سے قاضی کے فیصلہ کے ساتھ واپس کیا تو شفیع کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ یہ ہر اعتبار سے فتح ہے تو میرے لوٹ گیا بائع کی پرانی ملک کی جانب اور شفعہ انشاء عقد میں ہے اور اس میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے قبضہ کے درمیان اور عدم قبضہ کے درمیان ۔ تشریح زید نے بکر سے ایک مکان خریدا خالد کو حق شفعہ پہنچتا تھا مگر اس نے شفعہ لینے سے انکار کر دیا تو اب اس کا شفعہ باطل ہو چکا ہے۔ اب زید اس مکان کو واپس کرتا ہے یا تو خیار رویت کے سبب یا خیار شرط کے سبب یا عیب کے سبب اور عیب کی وجہ سے جب اس نے واپس کیا تو قاضی کے فیصلہ سے کیا۔ بہر حال جب ان تینوں صورتوں میں سے کسی صورت میں مکان مشتری کے پاس واپس آتا ہے تو خالد نے پھر شفعہ کا دعوی کر دیا یعنی بکر سے تو خالد نے انکار کر دیا تھا اور اب خالد زید سے اس کو شفعہ میں لینا چاہتا ہے اور اس واپسی کو بیچ کا درجہ دے کر شفعہ طلب کرتا ہے تو کیا خالد کو شفعہ ملے گا؟ تو فرمایا کہ نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ یہ بیچ نہیں بلکہ پہلی بیچ کا بالکلیہ فتح ہے تو جب شرط بالکلیہ فوت ہوگئی تو شفعہ ملنے کا کیا سوال؟ سوال یہاں بیج کسی اجنبی کے پاس نہیں آئی بلکہ بائع پہلے بھی اس کا مالک تھا اور اب بھی اس کا مالک ہے گویا کہ بائع کی ملک میں استمرار ہے اور استمرار کی صورت میں شفعہ نہیں ملتا اور کسی چیز کو اس کی سابق حالت پر واپس کرنے کی صورت میں شفعہ نہیں ملتا۔ بلکہ شفعہ انشاء عقد کی صورت میں ملتا ہے اور عقد کا انشاء یہاں ہے نہیں۔ پھر جب مشتری نے ان مذکورہ صورتوں میں مبیع کو واپس کیا تو یہی حکم ہے خواہ قبضہ سے پہلے واپس کرے یا قبضہ کے بعد ۔
When the buyer purchased a house, and the pre-emptor waived the pre-emption, then the buyer returned the house due to option of inspection or condition or defect by a judge's decree, then there is no pre-emption for the pre-emptor, because it is a rescission from every aspect, so it returns to the old ownership of the seller, and pre-emption is in the initiation of the contract. There is no difference in this between possession and non-possession. Explanation: Zaid bought a house from Bakr; Khalid had the right of pre-emption but he refused to take it, so his pre-emption is nullified. Now Zaid returns the house either due to khiyar al-ru'ya or khiyar al-shart or defect, and for defect he did it by qada. In any case, when the house comes back to (the seller) in any of these three ways, Khalid then claimed pre-emption again, i.e., he had refused from Bakr, and now he wants to take it from Zaid by pre-emption, treating the return as a sale. Will Khalid get pre-emption? He said: No, because this is not a sale but a complete rescission of the first sale. So when the condition (sale) is completely absent, how can pre-emption be claimed? Here the sale did not come to a stranger; rather the seller was the owner before and is still the owner, so there is continuity of ownership, and in continuity there is no pre-emption. Pre-emption is only in the initiation of a contract, and the initiation of a contract is not present here. And when the buyer returns the sold item in the mentioned ways, the same ruling applies whether the return is before or after possession.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof, covering the scenario where a pre-emptor initially waives his right, and then the buyer returns the property to the seller through a court judgment due to one of three options: khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection), khiyar al-shart (option of condition), or a defect (khiyar al-'ayb). The ruling: the pre-emptor's right does not revive. The proof is that such a return is a complete rescission (faskh) of the original sale, not a new sale. Pre-emption is only established upon the initiation of a contract (insha' al-'aqd) that transfers ownership to a new party. Here, the property returns to the original seller, so no new sale occurs. The commentary further clarifies that the return is not a sale; it is a nullification, so the condition for shuf'ah is absent. The same ruling applies whether the buyer had taken possession or not.

Key Terms
خیار رویت (khiyar al-ru'ya): Option of inspection: the buyer's right to annul the sale after seeing the purchased object if it was unseen at contract time.
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): Option of condition: a stipulated right to cancel the sale within a specified period.
خیار عیب (khiyar al-'ayb): Option of defect: the buyer's right to return the item if a pre-existing defect is discovered.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission: annulment of a contract retroactively, as if it never existed.
إنشاء العقد (insha' al-'aqd): Initiation of a contract: the formation of a new contract that transfers ownership or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, a pre-emptor who waived his right cannot later claim shuf'ah after the buyer returns the property due to khiyar al-shart because:
A) The pre-emptor's waiver is permanent and cannot be undone.
B) The return is a rescission of the original sale, not a new sale, and shuf'ah only arises from a new sale.
C) The return must be by a judge's decree, and without that decree the pre-emptor could claim.
D) The pre-emptor can only claim if the property is returned due to a defect, not due to khiyar al-shart.

Key Takeaway
A pre-emptor's waiver extinguishes his right permanently; a subsequent return of the property by the buyer via khiyar does not revive it because the return is a rescission, not a new sale.

Pre-emption After Return Without Qada or Iqalah
Ruling that pre-emptor gets shuf'ah after return without qada or iqalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shuf'ah when the buyer returns the property due to defect without a court judgment or by iqalah, and explain why it is considered a new sale for the pre-emptor.

Core Idea
A consensual return or iqalah is a new sale for the pre-emptor, preserving his right of shuf'ah.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a court-ordered return due to defect does not give shuf'ah. Now we examine the opposite: when the buyer returns the property without a court order, or the parties mutually rescind by iqalah. The Hanafi school rules that these actions do give shuf'ah. Why? Because what counts for the pre-emptor is the exchange of property by consent, which constitutes a sale for him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Locate the two cases: (1) buyer returns the sold property due to a defect without a court judgment, and (2) both parties mutually rescind the sale by iqalah.
These are distinct from a court-ordered return discussed earlier.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
The text rules that in both cases the pre-emptor (shafi') has the right of shuf'ah. It says: 'فللشفيع الشفعة' (so the shafi' has shuf'ah).
The ruling applies to both scenarios equally.
3
Understand the legal reasoning: rescission vs. new sale
For the parties themselves (buyer and seller), the return or iqalah is a rescission (فسخ) because they have authority over themselves. However, for a third party (the shafi'), the same transaction is considered a new sale because it involves the exchange of property by mutual consent.
The key distinction is that the parties' control does not extend to the pre-emptor.
4
Apply the definition of sale
The definition of a sale is 'exchange of property for property by mutual consent' (مبادلة المال بالمال بالتراضى). This definition is satisfied in these scenarios. Since the pre-emptor is a third party, he can base his claim on this new sale.
This reasoning is a form of qiyas: the transaction shares the effective cause (illa) of a sale for the third party.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وان ردها بعيب بغير قضاء او تقايلا البيع فللشفيع الشفعة لانه فسخ فى حقهما لولايتهما على انفسهما وقد قصد الفسخ وهو بيع جديد فى حق ثالث لوجود حد البيع وهو مبادلة المال بالمال بالتراضى والشفيع ثالث ومراده الرد بالعيب بعد القبض لان قبله فسخ من الاصل وان كان بغير قضاء على ما عرف
ترجمہ اور اگر واپس کیا مشتری نے گھر کو عیب کی وجہ سے بغیر قضاء کے یا دونوں نے بیج کا اقالہ کر لیا تو شفیع کیلئے شفعہ ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ان دونوں کے حق میں فتح ہے ان دونوں کی ولایت کی وجہ سے اپنے نفسوں پر حالانکہ ان دونوں نے فتح کا ارادہ کیا ہے اور تیسرے کے حق میں یہ جدید بیج ہے۔ بیع کی تعریف کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اور وہ رضا مندی کے ساتھ مال کو مال سے بدلنا ہے اور شفیع تیسرا ہی ہے اور اس کی مراد عیب کی وجہ سے قبضہ کے بعد واپس کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ قبضہ سے پہلے سرے سے فتح ہے۔ اگر چہ بغیر قضاء کے ہو اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو پہچان لیا گیا ہے۔

And if he returned it due to a defect without a court judgment, or they made iqalah of the sale, then the pre-emptor has shuf'ah, because it is a rescission in their own right due to their authority over themselves, and they intended rescission, and it is a new sale with respect to a third party because the definition of sale is present: exchanging property for property by mutual consent. The pre-emptor is a third party. And his intention is the return due to a defect after possession, because before possession it is a rescission from the beginning, even if without a judgment, as is known. Explanation: In the first case, return due to defect was by court judgment – its ruling has passed. But if the buyer returns the sold item due to defect without a court judgment, or they both make iqalah, then will the pre-emptor get shuf'ah? He said: In both these cases, shuf'ah will be given. Because here there is no court judgment; rather both have consented, and they are sane adults, competent over themselves, and they intend to rescind the sale. Therefore, their intention is valid regarding themselves. And it will be said that in their own right it is a rescission, but with respect to a third party it is a new sale. However, they have authority only over themselves, not over the pre-emptor; therefore their...

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, distinguishing two scenarios from the previous lesson. Here, the buyer returns the property due to defect without a court judgment (bighayr qada) or the parties mutually rescind by iqalah (mutual rescission). In these cases, the pre-emptor gets shuf'ah. The proof: although the return is a rescission in the eyes of the parties involved (because they have authority over themselves), it is considered a new sale vis-à-vis a third party (the pre-emptor). This is because the transaction fulfills the definition of a sale: mutual exchange of property by consent. The pre-emptor is a third party, so he can claim shuf'ah based on this new exchange. The commentary emphasizes that without a court judgment, the return is not compulsory; it is consensual, and thus it counts as a new sale for the pre-emptor. The missing part likely continues to clarify that the pre-emptor's right is established.

Key Terms
اقالہ (iqalah): Mutual rescission of a sale by both parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer returns a property due to a defect without a court judgment, does the pre-emptor get shuf'ah?
A) No, because it is a rescission.
B) Yes, because it is considered a new sale for a third party.
C) Yes, but only if the pre-emptor had not waived earlier.
D) No, because the defect return is invalid without court.

Key Takeaway
A consensual return or iqalah does not extinguish shuf'ah; it creates a new sale for the pre-emptor.

Shuf'ah Does Not Revive on Rescission of Sale
Ruling on shuf'ah when sale is rescinded by court order due to options or defect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shuf'ah when a sale is rescinded due to khiyar or defect and explain the legal distinction between faskh and a new sale.

Core Idea
A rescinded sale is not a new sale — shuf'ah does not revive when property returns to seller.

In Hanafi law, the right of preemption (shuf'ah) arises only upon a new transfer of ownership by sale. When a buyer returns the purchased property to the seller through rescission (faskh) due to khiyar al-ru'yah, khiyar al-shart, or a defect, the transaction is not a fresh sale but an annulment of the original contract. This lesson examines the ruling and reasoning behind why a preemptor who previously waived his right cannot reclaim it when the property comes back to the seller through such a rescission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage to identify the specific scenario: a buyer (Zaid) returns a house to the seller (Bakr) through one of three grounds (khiyar al-ru'yah, khiyar al-shart, or defect with court order). The preemptor (Khalid) had previously refused his right. Now Khalid claims shuf'ah again. The ruling is that shuf'ah is not granted.
2
Distinguish faskh from a new sale
The key legal concept is that the return is a complete rescission (faskh) of the original sale, not a new sale (insha' 'aqd). Shuf'ah is only triggered by a new transfer of ownership through a contract of sale. Since the property reverts to the seller's ownership as if the first sale never happened, there is no new transfer.
Faskh annuls the contract ab initio.
3
Apply the distinction to the three cases
The ruling applies equally to returns due to khiyar al-ru'yah, khiyar al-shart, and defect (adjudicated by a judge). In all cases, the return is considered faskh, not a new sale. Therefore, no shuf'ah arises.
Even if the buyer had taken possession, the ruling remains the same.
4
Note the consistency regardless of possession
The passage explicitly states that the same rule applies whether the return occurs before or after the buyer takes possession. This reinforces that the determinative factor is the nature of the transaction (faskh vs. new sale), not the timing of possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لو٘ٹ گیا بائع کی پرانی ملک کی جانب اور شفعہ انشاء عقد میں ہے اور اس میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے قبضہ کے درمیان اور عدم قبضہ کے درمیان ۔ تشریح زید نے بکر سے ایک مکان خریدا خالد کو حق شفعہ پہنچتا تھا مگر اس نے شفعہ لینے سے انکار کر دیا تو اب اس کا شفعہ باطل ہو چکا ہے۔ اب زید اس مکان کو واپس کرتا ہے یا تو خیار رویت کے سبب یا خیار شرط کے سبب یا عیب کے سبب اور عیب کی وجہ سے جب اس نے واپس کیا تو قاضی کے فیصلہ سے کیا۔ بہر حال جب ان تینوں صورتوں میں سے کسی صورت میں مکان مشتری کے پاس واپس آتا ہے تو خالد نے پھر شفعہ کا دعوی کر دیا یعنی بکر سے تو خالد نے انکار کر دیا تھا اور اب خالد زید سے اس کو شفعہ میں لینا چاہتا ہے اور اس واپسی کو بیچ کا درجہ دے کر شفعہ طلب کرتا ہے تو کیا خالد کو شفعہ ملے گا؟ تو فرمایا کہ نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ یہ بیچ نہیں بلکہ پہلی بیچ کا بالکلیہ فتح ہے تو جب شرط بالکلیہ فوت ہوگئی تو شفعہ ملنے کا کیا سوال؟ سوال یہاں بیج کسی اجنبی کے پاس نہیں آئی بلکہ بائع پہلے بھی اس کا مالک تھا اور اب بھی اس کا مالک ہے گویا کہ بائع کی ملک میں استمرار ہے اور استمرار کی صورت میں شفعہ نہیں ملتا اور کسی چیز کو اس کی سابق حالت پر واپس کرنے کی صورت میں شفعہ نہیں ملتا۔ بلکہ شفعہ انشاء عقد کی صورت میں ملتا ہے اور عقد کا انشاء یہاں ہے نہیں۔ پھر جب مشتری نے ان مذکورہ صورتوں میں مبیع کو واپس کیا تو یہی حکم ہے خواہ قبضہ سے پہلے واپس کرے یا قبضہ کے بعد ۔
Returned to the seller's former ownership, and preemption is in the initiation of a contract, and there is no difference between before and after possession. Explanation: Zaid bought a house from Bakr; Khalid had a right of shuf'ah but he refused it, so his shuf'ah is invalid. Now Zaid returns the house either due to khiyar al-ru'yah, khiyar al-shart, or due to a defect, and when he returned due to defect, it was by the judge's decision. In any of these three cases when the house comes back to the buyer (Zaid), Khalid claims shuf'ah again — i.e., he had refused from Bakr, and now he wants to take it in shuf'ah from Zaid, treating this return as a sale and seeking shuf'ah. So will Khalid get shuf'ah? It is said: No, because this is not a sale but a complete annulment of the first sale. So when the condition is completely lost, what question of shuf'ah? The property did not come to a stranger; the seller was its owner before and is its owner now, as if ownership continued. In case of continuity, shuf'ah is not given, and when something is returned to its previous state, shuf'ah is not given. Rather, shuf'ah is given in case of initiation of a contract, and there is no initiation here. Then when the buyer returns the sold property in these mentioned cases, the same rule applies whether he returns before or after possession.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This is a ruling passage explaining that when a buyer returns purchased property to the seller due to khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection), khiyar al-shart (option of condition), or a defect ('ayb) that was adjudicated by a judge, the preemptor (shafi') who had previously waived his right cannot revive it. The return is considered a complete rescission (faskh) of the original contract, not a new sale. Therefore, the condition for shuf'ah — a new transfer of ownership — is absent. The ruling is the same whether the return occurs before or after possession.

Key Terms
خيار رؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): Option of inspection; the buyer has the right to return the property upon seeing it if it does not match description.
خيار شرط (khiyar al-shart): Option of condition; a right to rescind the sale within a stipulated period.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment; rescission of a contract ab initio, not a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer returns a house to the seller due to a defect, and the return is ordered by a judge. Does the preemptor who previously refused his right get shuf'ah again?
A) Yes, because the property is transferred back.
B) No, because it is a complete rescission, not a new sale.
C) Yes, because the seller becomes owner again.
D) No, because the preemptor already refused.

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah attaches only to new contracts of sale (insha' 'aqd); a rescission (faskh) does not create a new transfer of ownership, so the preemptor's right does not revive.

Shuf'ah Revives on Iqalah or Return Without Court Order
Ruling with reasoning on shuf'ah after iqalah or return of defect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shuf'ah when a sale is rescinded by iqalah or return of defect without a judge, and explain the reasoning that distinguishes between faskh for the parties and a new sale for third parties.

Core Idea
Iqalah is a new sale for third parties, so shuf'ah revives even without a court order.

In the previous lesson, we learned that shuf'ah is lost when the sale is annulled by court order. But what if the annulment happens without a judge, by mutual consent (iqalah) or by the buyer returning a defective good? The Hanafi school holds that shuf'ah is reinstated in these cases. This lesson unpacks the subtle legal distinction between annulment for the contracting parties and a new sale for third parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage discusses two scenarios: (1) the buyer returns the purchased item to the seller due to a defect without a court order, and (2) the buyer and seller mutually rescind the sale (iqalah). In both cases, the original sale is annulled, but the ruling for shuf'ah changes.
The key condition is that the return occurs after possession (qabd). Before possession, the return is pure faskh.
2
State the ruling
In both scenarios, the preemptor (shafi') has the right of shuf'ah, i.e., the right to step into the buyer's place and acquire the property at the same price.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The text explains that the annulment (faskh) between the original parties is effective for themselves, but it is considered a new sale vis-à-vis third parties. The definition of a sale – exchange of property by mutual consent – is present, and the preemptor is a third party who was not party to the annulment agreement.
Hence, the preemptor cannot be bound by the parties' intention to annul, and the transaction is treated as a new sale for him.
4
Note the limitation
This ruling applies only when the return occurs after possession. If the defect is discovered before possession and the buyer returns the item, it is a complete annulment from the beginning, with no element of a new sale, so shuf'ah does not revive.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah makes this distinction clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ردها بعيب بغير قضاء او تقايلا البيع فللشفيع الشفعة لانه فسخ فى حقهما لولايتهما على انفسهما وقد قصد الفسخ وهو بيع جديد فى حق ثالث لوجود حد البيع وهو مبادلة المال بالمال بالتراضى والشفيع ثالث ومراده الرد بالعيب بعد القبض لان قبله فسخ من الاصل وان كان بغير قضاء على ما عرف... تشریح پہلی صورت میں عیب کی وجہ سے واپسی قاضی کے حکم سے تھی اس کا حکم گذر چکا اور اگر بغیر قاضی کے فیصلہ کے عیب کی وجہ سے مبیع کو واپس کر دیا ہو یا دونوں نے اقالہ کر لیا ہو تو اب شفیع کو شفعہ ملے گا یا نہیں؟ تو فرمایا کہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں شفعہ ملے گا۔ چونکہ یہاں قاضی کا حکم تو ہے نہیں بلکہ ان دونوں کی رضامندی ہے اور یہ دونوں عاقل بالغ ہیں اہل ولایت ہیں اپنے اوپر دونوں کو ولایت حاصل ہے اور ان دونوں نے بیع کو فسخ کرنے کا رادہ کیا ہے لہذا ان کی ذات تک ان کا ارادہ معتبر ہوگا۔ اور کہا جائے گا کہ ان دونوں کے حق میں یہ نخ بیج ہے۔ مگر ان کو اپنے اوپر ہی ولایت ہے شفیع کے اوپر نہیں لہذا ان کا رادہ شفیع کے اوپر نہیں تھوپا جا سکتا۔ بلکہ یہ کہا جائے گا کہ ان دونوں کے حق میں یہ نسخ ہے اور تیسرے کے حق میں بیج جدید ہے اور شفیع تیسرا ہی ہے اور بیع کہنے میں کچھ حرج بھی نہیں کیونکہ بیع کی تعریف موجود ہے۔ یعنی مبادلة المال بالمال بالتراضی ۔ بہر حال شفیع کو شفعہ ملے گا اور اقالہ کو یہ حکم پہلے سے جانا پہچانا ہے کہ وہ متعاقدین کے حق میں فتح اور ثالث کے حق میں بیچ جدید ہے۔ و مراده الرد.... الخ مگر یہ ساری تقریر اس وقت ہے جبکہ خیار عیب کی وجہ سے قبضہ کے بعد واپس کرے ورنہ اگر قبضہ سے پہلے ہی واپس کر دے تو اب یہ بالکلیہ نسخ ہے اور بیع جدید کا شائبہ اس کے اندر نہیں ہے لہذا اب شفیع کو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ کیونکہ خیار عیب کی وجہ سے اگر قبضہ کے بعد واپسی ہو تو صفقہ بیع کے بعد واپسی ہے جو بیع جدید ہو سکتی ہے اور قبضہ سے پہلے صفقہ ہی نام نہیں ہوا۔ لہذا اس کو مجبور بالکلیہ فسخ قرار دینا پڑے گا۔ مصنف نے ہدایہ ص ۲۳ ج ۳ پر یہی تقریر کی ہے لان الصفقة تم مع خيار العيب بعد القبض و ان كانت لانتم قبلہ اس کا حوالہ دیتے ہوئے فرما ر ہے ہیں علی ما عرف۔
And if he returns it due to a defect without a court order, or they mutually rescind the sale, then the preemptor has the right of shuf'ah because it is an annulment in their favor due to their authority over themselves, and they intended annulment, but it is a new sale for a third party because the definition of sale exists: exchange of property for property by mutual consent, and the preemptor is a third party. His intention is return due to defect after possession, because before possession it is an annulment from the beginning, even if without a court order according to what is known... Explanation: The first case of return due to defect by court order has been ruled upon. If he returns due to defect without a judge's decision or they do iqalah, does the preemptor get shuf'ah? He said: In these two cases, shuf'ah will be given. Since there is no court order here but their mutual consent, and they are sane adults with authority over themselves, and they intended to annul the sale, so their intention is valid regarding themselves. But they have authority only over themselves, not over the preemptor, so their intention cannot be imposed on the preemptor. Rather, it will be said that it is an annulment for them and a new sale for the third party, and the preemptor is the third party. There is no harm in calling it a sale because the definition of sale exists: exchange of property for property by mutual consent. In any case, the preemptor gets shuf'ah, and iqalah is known to be an annulment for the contractors and a new sale for a third party. All this discussion applies when he returns after possession due to khiyar al-'ayb. If he returns before possession, it is a complete annulment with no trace of a new sale, so the preemptor will not get shuf'ah, because after possession the transaction is concluded with khiyar al-'ayb, whereas before it is not.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-reasoning passage. The text presents the scenario where a buyer returns property to the seller due to a defect without a court order, or the two parties mutually rescind the sale (iqalah). In these cases, the preemptor's right revives. The reasoning is that although the contract is annulled (faskh) between the two original parties, it is considered a new sale vis-à-vis third parties (like the preemptor) because the definition of sale — exchange of property for property by mutual consent — is present. Since the preemptor is a third party, he can claim shuf'ah based on this new sale. The ruling applies only when the return occurs after possession; if it occurs before possession, it is a pure annulment and no new sale, so no shuf'ah.

Key Terms
إقالة (iqalah): Mutual rescission of a sale by both parties.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of a contract; here distinguished between absolute faskh and faskh that is treated as a new sale for others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer and seller mutually rescind a sale (iqalah) after possession, does the preemptor have the right of shuf'ah?
A) No, because iqalah is an annulment.
B) Yes, because iqalah is a new sale for third parties.
C) No, because the preemptor already waived his right.
D) Yes, only if the judge orders it.

Key Takeaway
Iqalah or return of defect without court order after possession creates a new sale for third parties, reviving the preemptor's right of shuf'ah.

No Shuf'ah in Division and Khiyar al-Ru'yah
Hadith quote from al-Jami' al-Saghir negating shuf'ah in division and khiyar al-ru'yah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that shuf'ah does not apply in division (qismah) or when a sale is rescinded under khiyar al-ru'yah, and identify the correct grammatical reading that preserves this ruling.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is a right of preemption in sales; it does not arise from division or return under khiyar al-ru'yah.

This lesson examines a crucial passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir, a foundational Hanafi text. The ruling is straightforward: no shuf'ah in division of joint property, and no shuf'ah when a sale is rescinded due to the option of inspection. However, the Arabic phrase can be misread, and we will explore why the Hanafi school insists on a specific grammatical reading to uphold the correct ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two negated cases
Read the hadith carefully: 'لا شفعة في قسمة ولا خيار رؤية'. Recognize that the negation applies to shuf'ah in both division (qismah) and khiyar al-ru'yah.
2
Understand the meaning of shuf'ah
Shuf'ah is a preemptive right to purchase a co-owner's share when it is sold to a third party. It is triggered by a sale, not by other property transactions.
3
Recognize the grammatical dispute
The word 'رؤية' can be read with kasra (ru'yah, genitive) or fatha (ru'yah, nominative). The reading changes the meaning: with kasra, 'لا شفعة في قسمة ولا في خيار رؤية' (no shuf'ah in division, nor in khiyar al-ru'yah). With fatha, it becomes 'لا شفعة في قسمة ولا خيار رؤية' (no shuf'ah in division and no khiyar al-ru'yah), which incorrectly negates the option itself.
The author (Sahib al-Hidayah) affirms the kasra reading.
4
Apply the correct reading
The correct interpretation is that shuf'ah is absent in both cases. Khiyar al-ru'yah itself is valid and established; it is the preemptive right that does not attach when a sale is rescinded under this option.
This is supported by the preserved narration in the book of division.
5
Explain the reasoning
Shuf'ah only arises from a sale that introduces a new co-owner. In division, existing co-owners simply separate shares; no new co-owner enters. In khiyar al-ru'yah, the return is a rescission (faskh), not a new sale. Hence, no shuf'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفى الجامع الصغير ولا شفعة في قسمة ولا خيار رؤية وهو بكسر الراء ومعناه لاشفعة بسبب الرد بخيار الرؤية لما بيناه ولا تصح الرواية بالفتح عطفا على الشفعة لان الرواية محفوظة فى كتاب القسمة انه يثبت في القسمة خيار الرؤية وخيار الشرط لانهما يثبتان لخلل فى الرضاء فيما يتعلق لزومه بالرضاء وهذا المعنى موجود في القسمة و الله سبحانه اعلم ترجمہ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے اور شفعہ نہیں ہے بٹوارہ میں اور نہ خیار رویت میں اور یہ ( خیار ) را کے کسرہ کے ساتھ ہے۔ جس کے معنی ہیں خیار رویت کی وجہ سے واپس کرنے کے سبب سے شفعہ نہیں ہے۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور فتح کے ساتھ روایت شفعہ پر عطف کرتے ہوئے صحیح نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ مبسوط کتاب القسمیہ میں محفوظ روایت ہے کہ بٹوارہ میں خیار رویت اور خیار شرط ثابت ہوتے ہیں۔ اسلئے کہ یہ دونوں ثابت ہوتے ہیں رضامندی کے اندر خلل کی وجہ سے ایسے عقد کے اندر جس کا لزوم رضا مندی کے ساتھ وابستہ ہے اور یہ معنی بنوارہ میں موجود ہیں واللہ سبحانہ اعلم ۔ تشریح متن کے مسائل سے فراغت کے بعد صاحب ہدایہ یہاں سے جامع صغیر کی ایک عبارت نقل فرما کر اس پر کچھ تبصرہ فرمائیں گے۔ جامع صغیر کی عبارت ولا شفعه في قسمة ولا خيار رؤية بؤارہ اور خیار رؤیت میں شفعہ نہیں ہے جس کا بیان ابھی گذر چکا ہے۔ خیار کا عطف قسمہ پر ہے یا شفعہ پر ۔ اول صورت میں راء پر کسرہ ہوگا اور دوسری صورت میں فتحہ ہوگا۔ بعض حضرات نے اس پر فتح پڑھا اور شفعہ پر اس کا عطف کیا اب اس کا مطلب یہ ہو جائے گا کہ ہوارہ میں شفعہ ہے اور نہ خیار رؤیت ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ یہ غلط ہے مبسوط کی کتاب القسمہ کی روایت اس کے خلاف موجود ہے کہ بٹوارہ میں شفعہ نہیں ہے اور نہ خیا رؤیت میں شفعہ ہے بہر حال اس وجہ سے اس کو مکسور پڑھنا پڑے گا۔
And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'There is no shuf'ah in division (qismah) nor in khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection).' It is with kasra on the ra, meaning: there is no shuf'ah due to return by khiyar al-ru'yah, as we explained. And the narration with fatha (reading 'ru'yah' as nominative) is not correct when conjuncted with shuf'ah, because the preserved narration in the book of division is that khiyar al-ru'yah and khiyar al-shart are established in division, because they are established due to a defect in consent regarding a contract whose binding is tied to consent, and this meaning exists in division. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage quotes al-Jami' al-Saghir to affirm two rulings: (1) There is no shuf'ah in division of jointly owned property (qismah). (2) There is no shuf'ah when a sale is rescinded due to khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection). The commentary discusses the correct reading of the phrase: whether 'khiyar' is in the nominative (raf') or genitive (jarr) case. The correct reading is with kasra on the ra of 'ru'yah', meaning it is genitive: 'nor in khiyar al-ru'yah'. Some scholars incorrectly read with fatha, making it nominative and conjoined to 'shuf'ah', implying that there is shuf'ah in division but not in khiyar al-ru'yah. The author (Sahib al-Hidayah) rejects this, citing that in the book of division, both khiyar al-ru'yah and khiyar al-shart are established. The point is that the preemptor's right does not arise from a return based on khiyar al-ru'yah, because that return is a rescission, not a new sale.

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners.
خيار رؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): Option of inspection; the right to return an unseen purchased item upon seeing it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Jami' al-Saghir, is there shuf'ah in division (qismah) of property?
A) Yes, shuf'ah applies in division.
B) No, there is no shuf'ah in division.
C) Only if the division is by sale.
D) Only if the preemptor consents.

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is a right specific to sales; it does not arise from property division or from a return under khiyar al-ru'yah.

Nullification of Shuf'ah by Neglecting Ishhad
Ruling with proof: shuf'ah nullified by neglecting ishhad when able.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which shuf'ah is nullified and apply the ability condition to distinguish valid excuses.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is lost only when the pre-emptor deliberately abandons demand despite being able to act.

This lesson examines the second section of shuf'ah: how it is nullified. Imam al-Quduri's ruling establishes that failure to perform the initial demand (talab al-muwahaba) when able causes the right to lapse. The key is that abandonment (i'rad) is inferred only from inaction during a state of free choice, which requires ability. We will walk through the ruling, its rationale, and the critical condition of ability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'neglecting ishhad upon learning of the sale while able.' The ruling: shuf'ah is nullified.
The ruling applies to the immediate demand (talab al-muwahaba), not later demands.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a rational principle: turning away (i'rad) only occurs in a state of choice, which is when ability exists.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the nature of choice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Inaction when able indicates deliberate turning away; if unable, inaction is not abandonment. The link is the inference of intention from behaviour.
The legal cause (illa) is the conscious decision to forgo the right.
4
Note the condition of ability
Ability (qudra) is essential: only when the shafi' is physically and legally capable does his inaction count as i'rad.
Incapacity preserves the right; the burden is on the shafi' to prove inability if contested.
5
Evaluate practical application
The shafi' must act immediately upon learning; any delay without excuse costs the right. This promotes certainty and prevents speculation.
Some schools fix a time limit; Hanafi ties nullification to active demand, not calendar time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما تبطل به الشفعة
ترجمہ یہ باب ان چیزوں کے بیان میں ہے جن سے شفعہ باطل ہو جاتا ہے
تشریح یہ بات یقینی ہے کہ ثبوت پہلے ہوتا ہے اور بطلان بعد میں اس لئے مصنف نے باب ما يثبت به الشفعة کو متقدم کیا اور باب ما تبطل به الشفعة کو مؤخر کیا ہے۔
طلب اشہاد کے چھوڑنے سے شفع کا حق باطل ہو جاتا ہے
قال واذا ترك الشفيع الاشهاد حين علم بالبيغ وهو يقدر على ذالك بطلت شفعته لإعراضه عن الطلب وهذا لان الاعراض انما يتحقق حالة الاختيار وهي عند القدرة
ترجمہ امام قدوری نے کہا کہ اور جبکہ شفیع نے اشہاد کو چھوڑ دیا جبکہ اس کو بیع کا علم ہوا ۔ حالانکہ اس پر قادر ہے تو اس کا شفعہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اس کے اعراض کرنے کی وجہ سے طلب سے اور یہ قدرت کی شرط لگانا ) اسلئے کہ اعراض اختیار ہی کی حالت میں متحقق ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہ ( حالت اختیار ) قدرت کے وقت ہے۔
تشریح امام قدوری کے کلام میں اشتہار سے مراد طلب اشہاد اور طلب تقریر نہیں ہے بلکہ طلب مواہبہ ہے۔ اب عبارت کا مطلب سنے شفیع کو بیع کا علم ہوا اور وہ طلب مواشبہ پر قادر ہے۔ اس سے عاجز نہ ہو اس کے باوجود بھی اس نے طلب مواہبہ نہیں کیا تو چونکہ یہ اعراض کی دلیل ہے اسلئے اس کا شفعہ باطل ہو گیا۔
اب سوال پیدا ہوا کہ دھو بقدر کی قید کیوں لگائی گئی ہے؟ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ جب شفیع قدرت کے باوجود سفعہ کی طلب کو چھوڑے گا تیبی تو اعراض ہو گا ورنہ بر بناء بجز تر کی وجہ سے اعراض کا حقق نہ ہوگا اور پھر شفعہ باطل نہ ہوگا۔
Section: What nullifies shuf'ah. Translation: This section is about the things that nullify shuf'ah. Commentary: It is certain that establishment comes first and nullification later, so the author placed the section 'What establishes shuf'ah' first and 'What nullifies shuf'ah' later. That shuf'ah is nullified by neglecting ishhad. He (Imam al-Quduri) said: If the shafi' (pre-emptor) abandons ishhad (witnessing) when he learns of the sale and he is able to do so, his shuf'ah is nullified due to his turning away from the demand. This is because turning away only occurs in a state of choice, which is when one has ability. Translation of Imam al-Quduri's statement: And when the shafi' leaves ishhad at the time he learns of the sale while he is able to do so, his shuf'ah becomes void because of his abandonment of demand. This is because abandonment only materializes in a state of free choice, and that is when there is ability. Commentary: In Imam al-Quduri's words, ishhar (noticing) here means demand for witness and demand for confirmation is not intended; rather, it is the demand for mushahaba (immediate request). Now the meaning: The shafi' learns of the sale and he is able to make the demand immediately; he is not incapable. Despite that, he does not make the immediate demand. Since this is evidence of abandonment, his shuf'ah becomes void. Now a question arises: Why is the condition of ability added? The answer: When the shafi' with ability leaves the demand of shuf'ah, then abandonment occurs. Otherwise, due to incapacity, abandonment does not occur, so shuf'ah is not nullified.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage introduces the section on nullification of shuf'ah. The author explains the logical order: first the section on how shuf'ah is established, then this section on how it is invalidated. Imam al-Quduri's ruling is presented: if the pre-emptor (shafi') becomes aware of a sale that triggers shuf'ah, and he has the ability to immediately perform ishhad (witnessing the demand), but he deliberately fails to do so, his right of shuf'ah is nullified. The reasoning is that his inaction indicates i'rad (turning away or abandonment) of his claim. The condition of ability is crucial: if he is unable (e.g., due to illness, absence, or fear), then abandonment is not inferred, and his right remains. The commentary further clarifies that the 'ishhad' mentioned here does not refer to the second type of demand (talab al-ishhad wa al-taqrir), but to the first type (talab al-muwahaba), which is the immediate demand made upon learning of the sale. Thus, if he fails to make this initial demand despite ability, his shuf'ah is lost. This underscores that the pre-emptor must act promptly; delay without excuse is fatal to the right.

Key Terms
شفيع (shafi'): The person entitled to pre-emption (co-owner or neighbor).
إشهاد (ishhad): The act of summoning witnesses to testify to the demand for shuf'ah.
إعراض (i'rad): Turning away; the pre-emptor's deliberate abandonment of his claim.
قدرة (qudra): Ability; the condition that must be present for abandonment to be deemed voluntary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a pre-emptor learns of a sale but is too ill to go to the property and demand shuf'ah?
A) His shuf'ah is nullified immediately.
B) His shuf'ah remains because he lacks the ability to demand.
C) He must send someone else or it is nullified.
D) He loses shuf'ah if he does not demand within three days.

Key Takeaway
The right of shuf'ah is nullified only when the pre-emptor deliberately abandons the immediate demand while able; inability excuses delay and preserves the right.

Why Khiyar al-Ru'ya and Khiyar al-Shart Combine in Shuf'a
Answering why two khiyar options coexist in pre-emption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rationale for combining khiyar al-ru'ya and khiyar al-shart in shuf'a and partition, and distinguish these from khiyar al-'ayb.

Core Idea
Contracts binding on consent require both khiyar al-ru'ya and khiyar al-shart to ensure clear satisfaction in shuf'a and partition.

In Hanafi fiqh, pre-emption (shuf'a) and partition (qismah) are contracts that become binding only when each party's consent is fully evident. That is why the law allows two key options—khiyar al-ru'ya (inspection) and khiyar al-shart (stipulation)—to coexist in these transactions. This lesson unpacks the reason from a classical text and clarifies how this differs from the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two khiyar options
Recall that khiyar al-ru'ya gives the buyer the right to rescind after seeing the object, while khiyar al-shart allows rescission within a specified period. Both aim to ensure consent.
These options are well-known in Hanafi sales law.
2
Grasp the underlying principle
The text states that certain contracts (shuf'a and partition) are binding only upon clear consent. Hence, options that verify consent are needed.
The principle is 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applied to consent.
3
Apply to shuf'a and partition
In shuf'a, the pre-emptor takes the property subject to the buyer's options. In partition, each party must be satisfied with the division. Thus both options remain operative.
The same rationale applies to both contexts.
4
Contrast with khiyar al-'ayb
Khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) is different—it arises from a hidden defect, not from uncertainty of consent. Its return procedure is separate and does not combine in the same way.
The text warns against conflating these.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوال ... لانها يثبتان .. الخ ہوارہ میں خیار رویت اور خیار شرط کیوں ملتے ہیں؟
كتاب الشفعة
جواب جن عقدوں کا لزوم رضا مندی پر ہوتا ہے تا کہ وہاں رضا مندی صاف طور پر معلوم ہو جائے اس وجہ سے یہ دونوں خیار ملتے ہیں اور یہ وجہ بٹوارہ کے اندر بھی موجود ہے اس وجہ سے یہ دونوں خیار ملیں گے۔ تنبیه خیار عیب اور خیار رویت اور خیار شرط کی وجہ سے واپس کرنا اور بوقت واپسی شفیع کا مطالبہ کرنا اور چیز ہے اور جس کیلئے خیار شرط ہے اور اس مدت میں اس کے برابر میں کوئی مکان فروخت ہو اور یہ اس میں شفعہ کا دعوی کرے یہ اور مسئلہ ہے جس کا بیان ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے۔ ایک سونے والے طالبعلم نے بیدار ہو کر مجھ سے یہی سوال سبق میں کیا تھا تو میں نے یہی جواب دیا۔
Question: Why do khiyar al-ru'ya and khiyar al-shart combine in this case? Answer: Contracts whose binding nature depends on consent, so that consent is clearly known, therefore these two options combine. And this reason also exists in partition, so these two options will combine. Warning: Returning due to khiyar al-'ayb, khiyar al-ru'ya, or khiyar al-shart, and the shafi'i's claim at the time of return is a different matter. And the case where someone has khiyar al-shart and during that period a property beside his is sold and he claims pre-emption is another issue already explained. A sleeping student awakened and asked me this same question in class, and I gave this same answer.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This is a conceptual explanation passage. The author addresses why two khiyar options—khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection) and khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation)—are both operative in shuf'a (pre-emption) and in partition (qismah). The rationale is that these contracts are binding only upon clear consent, and these options help ascertain that consent. In shuf'a, the right of pre-emption is established upon sale, but the buyer's consent must be verified, hence both options remain. Similarly, in partition, consent must be clear. The author then distinguishes this from khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect), which involves return due to a hidden defect and triggers a different procedure for the shafi'i's claim. He also notes a separate scenario where a person with khiyar al-shart may claim pre-emption on a neighboring property sold during the option period, which was explained earlier. Finally, he mentions a personal teaching anecdote.

Key Terms
خیار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): Option of inspection – the right to rescind a contract upon seeing the object if it does not meet expectations.
خیار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Option of stipulation – the right to rescind within a specified period as agreed in the contract.
شفعة (shuf'a): Pre-emption – the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold property by paying the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do khiyar al-ru'ya and khiyar al-shart combine in shuf'a according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because shuf'a is a binding contract that requires explicit consent from all parties.
B) Because these options are inherited from the seller, not from the buyer.
C) Because the purpose is to ensure clear consent, as the contract's binding depends on consent.
D) Because shuf'a is invalid without these options.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ru'ya and khiyar al-shart combine in shuf'a and partition to ensure clear consent, as these contracts are binding only upon satisfaction.

The Logical Priority of Establishment over Nullification in Shuf'a
Introduces the chapter and explains the order of topics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the chapter on nullification of pre-emption follows the chapter on establishment, and distinguish between the legal concepts of thubut (establishment) and butlan (nullification).

Core Idea
A right must be established before it can be nullified — this logical order shapes the structure of Hanafi legal texts.

This short passage from the introduction to the chapter on what nullifies pre-emption (shuf'a) reveals the systematic approach of Hanafi jurists. They did not arrange chapters arbitrarily but followed a logical sequence: first, how the right of pre-emption is established, then how it is voided. Understanding this sequence is key to mastering the fiqh of shuf'a and appreciating the methodological rigor of the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key terms
The passage mentions thubut (establishment) and butlan (nullification). Define each in the context of shuf'a.
2
Understand the temporal relationship
The commentary states that thubut comes first, butlan later. Recognize that logically, a right must exist before it can be nullified.
3
Apply to chapter ordering
The author placed the chapter on establishment before nullification because of this logical priority.
4
Generalize to legal methodology
This ordering reflects a broader principle: in fiqh, discussions of conditions and causes precede discussions of nullifiers and exceptions.
This step shows the systematic nature of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما تبطل به الشفعة
ترجمہ یہ باب ان چیزوں کے بیان میں ہے جن سے شفعہ باطل ہو جاتا ہے
تشریح یہ بات یقینی ہے کہ ثبوت پہلے ہوتا ہے اور بطلان بعد میں اس لئے مصنف نے باب ما يثبت به الشفعة کو متقدم کیا اور باب ما تبطل به الشفعة کو مؤخر کیا ہے۔
Chapter on what nullifies pre-emption. Translation: This chapter explains the things by which pre-emption becomes void. Elaboration: It is certain that establishment comes first and nullification later, so the author placed the chapter on what establishes pre-emption first and the chapter on what nullifies pre-emption later.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This is a chapter introduction passage. The author explains the logic behind the ordering of chapters: since a right must be established before it can be nullified, the chapter on establishment of shuf'a precedes this chapter on nullification. This reflects a logical sequence in legal exposition.

Key Terms
ثبوت (thubut): Establishment of the right of pre-emption.
بطلان (butlan): Nullification or voidance of the right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Hanafi jurists arrange legal topics in a logical order: first how a right is established, then how it is nullified.

When Omitting Demand for Witnessing Voids Pre-emption
Ruling on the consequence of omitting formal demand for witnessing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that omitting talaab al-ishhad when able nullifies shuf'a and apply the condition of ability to determine when the right is preserved.

Core Idea
Omission of demand only voids pre-emption when the shafi'i had the ability to demand.

In this passage, Imam al-Quduri lays down a critical rule for the right of pre-emption (shuf'a): the shafi'i must formally demand witnessing (talaab al-ishhad) once he learns of the sale. If he fails to do so while able, his right is lost. The key nuance is the condition of ability – without it, mere omission does not prove abandonment. We will unpack the ruling, its reasoning, and a related scenario to ensure you grasp when the right is truly voided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the first part of the passage: the right of shuf'a becomes void when the shafi'i leaves talaab al-ishhad. This is the basic legal outcome.
2
Spot the condition – ability
Notice the phrase 'when he is able to do so' (وهو يقدر على ذلك). The ruling applies only if the shafi'i had the capacity (qudra) to make the demand. No ability, no void.
This condition prevents injustice to those who are genuinely unable.
3
Understand the rationale – turning away
The text explains that omission when able constitutes i'rad (turning away) from the right. I'rad is a voluntary act of abandonment that legally nullifies the claim.
If unable, the omission is not voluntary, so no turning away.
4
Apply to similar scenarios
The passage extends the ruling: even if the shafi'i makes a general demand in the gathering but fails to specifically demand before one of the contracting parties or at the property, the right is also void. The same logic of abandonment applies.
The demand must be specific and properly witnessed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طلب اشہاد کے چھوڑنے سے شفع کا حق باطل ہو جاتا ہے
قال واذا ترك الشفيع الاشهاد حين علم بالبيغ وهو يقدر على ذالك بطلت شفعته لإعراضه عن الطلب وهذا لان الاعراض انما يتحقق حالة الاختيار وهي عند القدرة
ترجمہ امام قدوری نے کہا کہ اور جبکہ شفیع نے اشہاد کو چھوڑ دیا جبکہ اس کو بیع کا علم ہوا ۔ حالانکہ اس پر قادر ہے تو اس کا شفعہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اس کے اعراض کرنے کی وجہ سے طلب سے اور یہ قدرت کی شرط لگانا ) اسلئے کہ اعراض اختیار ہی کی حالت میں متحقق ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہ ( حالت اختیار ) قدرت کے وقت ہے۔
تشریح امام قدوری کے کلام میں اشتہار سے مراد طلب اشہاد اور طلب تقریر نہیں ہے بلکہ طلب مواہبہ ہے۔ اب عبارت کا مطلب سنے شفیع کو بیع کا علم ہوا اور وہ طلب مواشبہ پر قادر ہے۔ اس سے عاجز نہ ہو اس کے باوجود بھی اس نے طلب مواہبہ نہیں کیا تو چونکہ یہ اعراض کی دلیل ہے اسلئے اس کا شفعہ باطل ہو گیا۔
اب سوال پیدا ہوا کہ دھو بقدر کی قید کیوں لگائی گئی ہے؟ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ جب شفیع قدرت کے باوجود سفعہ کی طلب کو چھوڑے گا تیبی تو اعراض ہو گا ورنہ بر بناء بجز تر کی وجہ سے اعراض کا حقق نہ ہوگا اور پھر شفعہ باطل نہ ہوگا۔
متبایعین اور عقار پر طلب اشہاد نہیں کیا تو شفعہ کا حق باطل ہے
وكذالك ان اشهد فى المجلس ولم يشهد على احد المتبايعين ولا عند العقار وقد اوضحناه فيما تقدم ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی اگر اس نے مجلس میں اشتہاد کی اور متبایعین میں سے کسی کے پاس اشہاد نہیں کیا اور نہ زمین کے پاس اور ہم اس کی ماقبل میں وضاحت کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح طلب کی اقسام ثلاثہ کا بیان ماقبل میں گزر چکا ہے تو مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ طلب مواہبہ کرنے کے بعد اگر اس نے طلب اشہاد کو چھوڑ دیا تب بھی شفعہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔
The right of pre-emption becomes void by leaving talaab al-ishhad. He said: If the shafi'i leaves talaab al-ishhad when he knows of the sale and is able to do so, his shuf'a is void due to his turning away from the demand. This is because turning away only occurs in a state of choice, which is when one has ability. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: When the shafi'i leaves ishhad while he has knowledge of the sale and is able, his shuf'a becomes void due to his turning away from the demand. The condition of ability is because turning away happens only in a state of choice, and that state of choice is when one has ability. Elaboration: In Imam al-Quduri's words, 'ishhad' here refers to talaab al-muwahaba (initial demand for readiness), not talaab al-ishhad (demand for witnessing) or talaab al-taqrir (demand for confirmation). The meaning: the shafi'i knew of the sale and was able to make the initial demand, not incapacitated, yet he did not do so. Since this is evidence of turning away, his shuf'a is void. A question arises: why is the condition of ability mentioned? The answer: when the shafi'i is able but leaves the demand, that constitutes turning away; otherwise, if he is unable, turning away does not occur and shuf'a is not void. And similarly, if he witnesses in the council but does not witness with one of the two parties nor at the property, his right is void. Translation: And likewise if he witnesses in the council but does not witness with one of the two contracting parties nor at the property, and we have clarified this earlier. Elaboration: The three types of demand were explained earlier; the author says that after making the initial demand, if he leaves the demand for witnessing, even then his shuf'a becomes void.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This is a ruling passage. The text presents the ruling from Imam al-Quduri that if the shafi'i (the person entitled to pre-emption) fails to make a formal demand for witnesses (talaab al-ishhad) when he has knowledge of the sale and has the ability to do so, his right of pre-emption is nullified. The reasoning is that such omission indicates i'rad (turning away) from the right. The author clarifies that 'ishhad' here means the initial demand (talaab al-muwahaba), not the subsequent demands. The condition of ability is crucial: if the shafi'i is unable (e.g., due to illness or absence), his omission does not constitute turning away and the right remains. The text then extends this: if the shafi'i makes the demand in the general gathering but fails to make it specifically before one of the contracting parties or at the property itself, the right is also void. This is consistent with the earlier discussion of the three types of demand (talaab al-muwahaba, talaab al-ishhad, talaab al-taqrir). The commentary reiterates that after making the initial demand, failing to follow up with the demand for witnessing nullifies the right.

Key Terms
طلب اشہاد (talaab al-ishhad): The demand for witnessing – the second stage of demand where the shafi'i asks witnesses to bear testimony to his claim.
اعراض (i'rad): Turning away or abandonment of the right, which legally nullifies shuf'a.
قدرت (qudra): Ability or capacity to make the demand; without it, omission is excused.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) If the shafi'i does not demand within three days.

Key Takeaway
The right of pre-emption is voided only when the shafi'i omits the formal demand for witnessing while having the ability to act; inability preserves the right.

Compromising Shuf'a for Consideration Nullifies It
Ruling on the validity of settling shuf'a for a payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a shafi'i accepts payment to drop his right of pre-emption and explain why the payment is invalid and must be returned.

Core Idea
Shuf'a rights cannot be sold; taking payment to drop them is bribery.

In this lesson, we examine a common scenario in property transactions: a shafi'i (holder of pre-emption right) agrees to drop his claim in exchange for a payment from the buyer. The Hanafi ruling is clear: such a settlement is invalid, the right is lost, and the payment must be returned. The underlying reasoning distinguishes between a proprietary right and a mere right to acquire ownership, which has significant implications for how we understand shuf'a.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction
The shafi'i makes a settlement (musalahah) with the buyer, agreeing to drop his right of shuf'a for a specific consideration (e.g., a sum of money).
2
State the ruling
According to Imam al-Quduri, the shuf'a becomes void (batil) and the consideration must be returned to the buyer.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The right of shuf'a is not a fixed proprietary right in the property; it is merely a right to become owner by paying the price. Since the shafi'i does not yet own the property, accepting payment for relinquishing the right is like taking a bribe (rishwah).
4
Consequence of the ruling
The shafi'i loses his shuf'a right entirely and must give back the payment. The buyer recovers the money, and the original sale stands.
5
Distinguish the valid dropping
If the shafi'i simply drops his right without any consideration, the action is valid and the right is lost without any payment issues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كسي عوض پر شفعہ سے دست برداري اختيار كي تو شفعہ نہيں ملے گا اور وہ عوض بھي رد كرنالازم ہے
قال وان صالح من شفعته على عوض بطلت شفعته ورد العوض لان حق الشفعة ليس بحق متقرر في المحل بل هو مجرد حق التملك فلا يصح الاعتياض عنه
ترجمہ: امام قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر اپنے شفعہ سے کسی عوض کے اوپر مصالحت کر لی تو اس کا شفعہ باطل ہو گیا اور عوض کو واپس کرے گا اسلئے
که حق شفعہ کوئی ایسا حق نہیں ہے جو کل کے اندر ثابت و منتظر رہو بلکہ حق شفعہ تو محض مالک بننے کا حق ہے تو اس کا عوض لینا صحیح نہ ہو گا۔ تشریح کسی شفیع نے مشتری سے مصالحت کی کہ میں ایک ہزار میں اپنا حق شفعہ چھوڑ دوں گا۔ لہذا مشتری نے شفیع کو ایک ہزار روپے دے دیئے تو اب کیا حکم ہے۔
تو فرمایا کہ شفعہ بھی باطل ہو گیا اور جو ہزار روپے لئے ہیں ان کا بھی واپس کرنا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ رشوت ہے جو حرام ہے کیوں؟ اسلئے کہ حق شفعہ میں شفیع کو اتنا حق ہے کہ وہ عوض دے کر دار مشفوعہ کا مالک بن جائے یعنی اس کیلئے صرف مالک بنے کا حق ہے۔ ایسی بات نہیں کہ دار مشفوعہ کے اندر شفیع کا کوئی ایسا حق ہے جو اس گھر میں ثابت شدہ ہو۔ بالفاظ دیگر شفیع اس کا مالک نہیں بنا صرف بن سکتا ہے
اور مالک بننے سے پہلے وہ عوض کس چیز کالے گا۔ لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ محض حق شفعہ کا عوض لینا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
If he chooses to withdraw from his shuf'a for a consideration, then shuf'a will not be granted and that consideration must also be returned. He said: If he settles regarding his shuf'a for a consideration, his shuf'a is void and the consideration is returned because the right of pre-emption is not a fixed right in the property, but rather it is a mere right to become owner, so taking consideration in exchange for it is not valid. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: If he makes a settlement (sulh) concerning his shuf'a for a consideration, his shuf'a is void and he must return the consideration, because the right of pre-emption is not a right that is established and permanent in the property, but rather it is merely a right to become owner, so taking compensation for it is not valid. Elaboration: A shafi'i made a settlement with the buyer: 'I will give up my right of pre-emption for one thousand,' so the buyer gave him one thousand rupees. What is the ruling? It was said: shuf'a is void and the one thousand rupees taken must also be returned because it is bribery, which is unlawful. Why? Because the shafi'i's right is only to become owner by paying the price; there is no established right in the property itself. In other words, he is not an owner but can become one. Before becoming owner, what consideration would he take? Therefore, taking consideration for the mere right of shuf'a is not valid.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This is a ruling passage. The text addresses a scenario where the shafi'i (one with the right of pre-emption) agrees to drop his claim in exchange for a payment from the buyer. The ruling is that such a settlement is invalid: the shafi'a right is nullified, but the payment taken must be returned. The reasoning is that the right of shuf'a is not a proprietary right already attached to the property; rather, it is merely a right to acquire ownership by paying the price. Since the shafi'i does not own the property, accepting compensation for relinquishing the right is like accepting bribery (rishwah), which is impermissible. The payment is therefore treated as unlawful and must be returned to the buyer. The ruling emphasizes that the shuf'a right cannot be sold or compensated; it can only be exercised or dropped without consideration.

Key Terms
مصالحة (musalahah): Settlement or compromise between the shafi'i and the buyer for dropping the right in exchange for something.
عوض (iwad): Consideration or payment given in exchange for the right of shuf'a.
رشوت (rishwah): Bribery – the payment is considered unlawful because it is for a right that cannot be sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a shafi'i accepts money from the buyer to drop his right of pre-emption?
A) The shuf'a right is void and the money is halal for the shafi'i.
B) The shuf'a right remains and the money must be returned.
C) The shuf'a right is void and the money must be returned as it is unlawful.
D) The shuf'a right becomes transferred to the buyer.

Key Takeaway
The right of shuf'a cannot be sold or compensated; any settlement for consideration is void and the payment must be returned as it is akin to bribery.
