Dropping Shuf'a Is Valid Even with Invalid Condition
Ruling on the effect of a condition when dropping shuf'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the effect of attaching a condition when dropping shuf'a and distinguish between valid and invalid conditions.

Core Idea
Dropping shuf'a is effective by the utterance alone — attached conditions do not affect its validity.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common confusion: if someone drops their right of pre-emption (shuf'a) but attaches a condition, does that invalidate the dropping? The ruling clarifies that the dropping stands independently, while the condition is assessed separately. Understanding this principle prevents errors in property transactions where a waiver of shuf'a is involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act in question is 'isqat' — dropping or relinquishing the right of shuf'a. Recognize that this is a unilateral declaration, not a contract.
2
Recognize the basis of validity
The dropping is effective by the verbal statement alone. The text states: 'its dropping is connected to his statement: I dropped my right.'
3
Distinguish between shart ja'iz and shart fasid
A valid condition (shart ja'iz) does not involve financial compensation; an invalid condition (shart fasid) does. Examples: 'provided seller does not demand price' vs. 'provided you give me 1000 rupees.'
4
Apply the rule
Whether the condition is valid or invalid, the dropping remains valid. The condition is evaluated separately: if valid it stands, if invalid it is void and any consideration must be returned.
The author uses a fortiori reasoning: if dropping is not connected to a valid condition, then even less so to an invalid one.
5
Note the practical consequence
The shafi'i cannot reclaim his right after dropping it, even if the condition is invalid. The condition's invalidity does not revive the right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شفعہ کا حق جائز شرط سے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے تو شرط فاسد سے بطریق اولی فاسد ہو جائے گا
ولا يتعلق اسقاطه بالجائز من الشرط فبالفاسد اولى فيبطل الشرط ويصح الاسقاط ترجمہ اور متعلق نہیں ہوتا حق شفعہ کا اسقاط جائز شرط کے ساتھ تو فاسد کے ساتھ بدرجہ اولی تو شرط باطل ہو جائے گی اور اسقاط صحیح ہوگا۔
تشریح شرط فاسد وہ ہے جس میں مال کا ذکر ہو اور جس میں مال کا ذکر نہ ہو وہ شرط جائز ہے۔ مثلہ شفیع نے مشتری سے کہا کہ میں نے اپنا حق شفعہ ساقط کر دیا اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ بائع مجھ سے شمن کا مطالبہ نہ کرے تو ظاہر ہے کہ جب شفیع دار مشفوعہ کو لے گا نہیں تو بائع یا مشتری شفیع سے شمن کا مطالبہ کیسے کریں گے۔ خلاصہ کلام یہ شرط جائز ہے اور اگر شفیع نے کہا کہ میں نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا اس شرط پر کہ تو مجھے ہزار روپے دے دے تو یہ شرط فاسد ہے۔ اب عبارت کا مطلب سمجھئے فرماتے ہیں کہ حق شفعہ کو ساقط کرنے کا کوئی تعلق شرط کے ساتھ نہیں ہے۔ خواہ شرط جائز ہو یا نا بد بلکہ اس کے اسقاط کا تعلق اس کے اس قول سے ہے کہ میں نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا۔
تو مصنف نے فرمایا کہ جب شرط جائز کے ساتھ حق شفعہ کے اسقاط کا تعلق نہیں ہے تو شرط فاسد کے ساتھ بدرجہ اولی نہ ہوگا ۔ بہر حال جب ایسا کر لیا تو کیا ہوگا ؟ تو جواب دیا کہ شرط باطل ہو جائے گی یعنی عوض کو واپس کرنا پڑے گا اور اسقاط صحیح ہو گا یعنی جو اس نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا تو وہ قو
The right of shuf'a falls by a valid condition; then by an invalid condition, a fortiori, it becomes invalid. And its dropping is not dependent on a valid condition, so by an invalid condition a fortiori, the condition becomes void and the dropping is valid. Translation: And the dropping of the right of shuf'a is not connected to a valid condition, so by an invalid condition a fortiori, the condition becomes void and the dropping is valid. Elaboration: An invalid condition is one that mentions wealth, and a condition that does not mention wealth is valid. For example, the shafi'i said to the buyer: 'I drop my right of shuf'a on condition that the seller does not demand the price from me.' Obviously, when the shafi'i does not take the property, how would the seller or buyer demand the price? In summary, this condition is valid. And if the shafi'i said: 'I drop my right on condition that you give me one thousand rupees,' then this condition is invalid. Now understand the meaning: He says that the dropping of the right of shuf'a has no connection with the condition, whether the condition is valid or not. Rather, its dropping is connected to his statement: 'I dropped my right.' So the author said: When the dropping of the right of shuf'a is not connected to a valid condition, then a fortiori it is not connected to an invalid condition. In any case, when this is done, what happens? The answer: The condition becomes void, meaning the consideration must be returned, and the dropping is valid, meaning what he dropped of his right remains effective.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This is a ruling passage on the effect of attaching a condition when dropping the right of shuf'a. The rule is that the dropping (isqat) of shuf'a is not dependent on any condition, whether valid or invalid. If the shafi'i utters the dropping, it takes effect regardless of any condition he attaches. The condition itself is evaluated separately: if it is valid (e.g., not involving money), it stands but does not affect the dropping; if it is invalid (e.g., requiring payment), the condition is void and any consideration given must be returned, but the dropping of the right remains valid. The author illustrates with examples: a valid condition is like saying 'I drop my right provided the seller does not demand the price' (which is moot since he is not taking the property). An invalid condition is like demanding payment for dropping. The key principle is that the dropping is by the oral statement alone, not by the condition. Thus, the shafi'i cannot sell his right; he can only drop it unconditionally.

Key Terms
اسقاط (isqat): Dropping or relinquishing the right of pre-emption.
شرط جائز (shart ja'iz): A valid condition that does not involve financial compensation.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): An invalid condition that involves financial compensation or is otherwise prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a shafi'i drops his right of shuf'a on condition that the buyer pays him one thousand rupees, what is the ruling?
A) Both the dropping and condition are valid.
B) The dropping is invalid and the payment must be returned.
C) The dropping is valid, but the condition is void and the payment must be returned.
D) The condition is valid but the dropping is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Dropping shuf'a is valid regardless of attached conditions; only the condition itself is evaluated and, if invalid, voided.

Relinquishing Shuf'ah for a Consideration Invalidates It
States ruling and reason for invalidating shuf'ah when exchanged for compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on relinquishing shuf'ah for a consideration and explain the legal rationale based on the distinction between haqq mutaqarrir and haqq al-tamalluk.

Core Idea
A right to become owner cannot be sold — shuf'ah is merely a potential, not property.

The right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) allows a co-owner or neighbour to step into a sale and purchase the property. But can this right itself be traded? The Hanafi school says no, and this lesson unpacks the legal reasoning: because shuf'ah is not an established property right, any payment for relinquishing it is invalid and must be returned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the source passage and extract the ruling: what happens if the pre-emptor makes a settlement (sulh) to abandon shuf'ah for a sum of money?
2
Understand the nature of shuf'ah
The passage explains that shuf'ah is not an established right (haqq mutaqarrir) in the property, but only a right to acquire ownership (haqq al-tamalluk). Grasp this distinction.
An established right, like ownership, can be exchanged for compensation; a mere potential right cannot.
3
Apply the legal principle
Since shuf'ah is not property, taking money for it is akin to a bribe (rishwah) and is haram. Therefore, the consideration must be returned, and the shuf'ah becomes void.
4
Conclude the operative ruling
The mufta bihi position: the relinquishment for consideration is batil (void), and the amount received must be returned. No compensation is permissible.
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان صالح من شفعته على عوض بطلت شفعته ورد العوض لان حق الشفعة ليس بحق متقرر في المحل بل هو مجرد حق التملك فلا يصح الاعتياض عنه
ترجمہ: امام قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر اپنے شفعہ سے کسی عوض کے اوپر مصالحت کر لی تو اس کا شفعہ باطل ہو گیا اور عوض کو واپس کرے گا اسلئے که حق شفعہ کوئی ایسا حق نہیں ہے جو کل کے اندر ثابت و منتظر رہو بلکہ حق شفعہ تو محض مالک بننے کا حق ہے تو اس کا عوض لینا صحیح نہ ہو گا۔ تشریح کسی شفیع نے مشتری سے مصالحت کی کہ میں ایک ہزار میں اپنا حق شفعہ چھوڑ دوں گا۔ لہذا مشتری نے شفیع کو ایک ہزار روپے دے دیئے تو اب کیا حکم ہے۔ تو فرمایا کہ شفعہ بھی باطل ہو گیا اور جو ہزار روپے لئے ہیں ان کا بھی واپس کرنا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ رشوت ہے جو حرام ہے کیوں؟ اسلئے کہ حق شفعہ میں شفیع کو اتنا حق ہے کہ وہ عوض دے کر دار مشفوعہ کا مالک بن جائے یعنی اس کیلئے صرف مالک بنے کا حق ہے۔ ایسی بات نہیں کہ دار مشفوعہ کے اندر شفیع کا کوئی ایسا حق ہے جو اس گھر میں ثابت شدہ ہو۔ بالفاظ دیگر شفیع اس کا مالک نہیں بنا صرف بن سکتا ہے اور مالک بننے سے پہلے وہ عوض کس چیز کالے گا۔ لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ محض حق شفعہ کا عوض لینا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
He said: And if one makes a settlement (sulh) regarding his right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) for a consideration (iwad), his pre-emption becomes void, and the consideration is to be returned, because the right of pre-emption is not an established right (haqq mutaqarrir) in the property (mahall), but rather it is merely a right to acquire ownership (haqq al-tamalluk); thus taking compensation for it is not valid. Commentary: Imam al-Quduri said: and if one makes a sulh regarding his pre-emption for a consideration, his pre-emption becomes void and he must return the consideration, because the right of pre-emption is not a right that is established and fixed in total; rather, the right of pre-emption is merely a right to become owner, so taking compensation for it is not valid. Explanation: A shafi' (pre-emptor) made a sulh with the purchaser (mushtari) saying, 'I will give up my right of pre-emption for one thousand.' The purchaser gave the shafi' one thousand rupees. What is the ruling? It is said: the pre-emption is void and the one thousand rupees taken must be returned, because this is bribery (rishwah) which is haram. Why? Because the right of pre-emption gives the shafi' only the right to become owner of the property (dar mashfu'ah) by paying its price; that is, he only has the right to become owner. It is not the case that the shafi' has an established right (haqq thabit) in the property. In other words, the shafi' has not become owner; he can only become owner. Before becoming owner, what is he taking compensation for? Thus it is understood that merely taking compensation for the right of pre-emption is not valid.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the invalidity of relinquishing the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) for a monetary consideration. The passage type is a ruling with rational proof. The author, Al-Quduri, states that if the pre-emptor (shafi') makes a settlement (sulh) with the purchaser (mushtari) whereby he abandons his right in exchange for a sum of money, the pre-emption is nullified and the amount received must be returned. The reason given is that the right of shuf'ah is not an established property right (haqq mutaqarrir) in the property itself; it is merely a right to acquire ownership (haqq al-tamalluk). Since it is not yet property, exchanging it for money is akin to taking a bribe (rishwah), which is haram. The commentary elaborates that the shafi' does not own the property; he only has the potential to own it by paying the price. Therefore, any payment received for relinquishing this right is invalid and must be returned. This ruling is based on rational analogy: one cannot sell a right that is not property. The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that relinquishment for consideration is void, and the consideration must be returned.

Key Terms
حق الشفعة (haqq al-shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption – the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase property that has been sold to an outsider.
حق متقرر (haqq mutaqarrir): An established, fixed right that is inherent in the property (e.g., ownership or qisas).
حق التملك (haqq al-tamalluk): A right to become owner, as opposed to actual ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is taking compensation for relinquishing the right of shuf'ah invalid in the Hanafi school?
A) Because the right of shuf'ah is a property right that cannot be exchanged
B) Because the right of shuf'ah is only a right to acquire ownership, not an established right in the property
C) Because the purchaser already owns the property and cannot pay for relinquishment
D) Because the sale of shuf'ah is prohibited by the Qur'an

Key Takeaway
Relinquishing a right that is merely a potential to own is not a valid exchange; any consideration received must be returned and the right becomes void.

Effect of Conditions on Relinquishing Shuf'ah
Explains that isqat of shuf'ah is independent of conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the validity of relinquishing shuf'ah when attached to a valid or invalid condition, and explain the consequence for the condition.

Core Idea
Relinquishment of shuf'ah is valid regardless of any condition; only the condition itself may be void.

This lesson clarifies a common confusion in the law of pre-emption (shuf'ah): when a person waives their right, does a condition attached to that waiver affect its validity? The Hanafi school, as presented in this text from Al-Quduri, draws a clear distinction between the act of relinquishment and the condition that accompanies it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is isqat (relinquishment) of the right of shuf'ah. According to the Hanafi school, this act is valid (sahih) per se, regardless of any conditions.
The ruling is unconditional: the relinquishment itself takes effect immediately.
2
Classify the type of condition
A condition is either jaa'iz (valid, not involving a financial exchange) or fasid (invalid, involving a financial exchange). The text gives examples: 'seller does not demand price' is valid; 'pay me 1000 rupees' is invalid.
The key is whether the condition involves mal (property).
3
Apply the ruling to the condition
Because the relinquishment is not connected to (muta'alliq) any condition – whether valid or invalid – the condition does not affect the validity of the isqat. The condition itself is evaluated separately: a valid condition remains, an invalid condition is void (yabtul).
The author uses an a fortiori argument: if a valid condition doesn't affect it, an invalid one certainly does.
4
Determine the practical outcome
In all cases, the relinquishment is valid. If the condition is invalid, any consideration (e.g., money) given for the condition must be returned. The condition is void but the isqat stands.
This prevents abuse: no one can 'sell' the right of shuf'ah by attaching an invalid condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يتعلق اسقاطه بالجائز من الشرط فبالفاسد اولى فيبطل الشرط ويصح الاسقاط
ترجمہ: اور متعلق نہیں ہوتا حق شفعہ کا اسقاط جائز شرط کے ساتھ تو فاسد کے ساتھ بدرجہ اولی تو شرط باطل ہو جائے گی اور اسقاط صحیح ہوگا۔ تشریح شرط فاسد وہ ہے جس میں مال کا ذکر ہو اور جس میں مال کا ذکر نہ ہو وہ شرط جائز ہے۔ مثلہ شفیع نے مشتری سے کہا کہ میں نے اپنا حق شفعہ ساقط کر دیا اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ بائع مجھ سے شمن کا مطالبہ نہ کرے تو ظاہر ہے کہ جب شفیع دار مشفوعہ کو لے گا نہیں تو بائع یا مشتری شفیع سے شمن کا مطالبہ کیسے کریں گے۔ خلاصہ کلام یہ شرط جائز ہے اور اگر شفیع نے کہا کہ میں نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا اس شرط پر کہ تو مجھے ہزار روپے دے دے تو یہ شرط فاسد ہے۔ اب عبارت کا مطلب سمجھئے فرماتے ہیں کہ حق شفعہ کو ساقط کرنے کا کوئی تعلق شرط کے ساتھ نہیں ہے۔ خواہ شرط جائز ہو یا نا بد بلکہ اس کے اسقاط کا تعلق اس کے اس قول سے ہے کہ میں نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا۔ تو مصنف نے فرمایا کہ جب شرط جائز کے ساتھ حق شفعہ کے اسقاط کا تعلق نہیں ہے تو شرط فاسد کے ساتھ بدرجہ اولی نہ ہوگا ۔ بہر حال جب ایسا کر لیا تو کیا ہوگا ؟ تو جواب دیا کہ شرط باطل ہو جائے گی یعنی عوض کو واپس کرنا پڑے گا اور اسقاط صحیح ہو گا یعنی جو اس نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا تو وہ قو ساقط ہو گیا مگر عوض کو واپس کرنا پڑے گا۔
And the relinquishment (isqat) of it (shuf'ah) is not connected to (muta'alliq) a valid (jaa'iz) condition, so with an invalid (fāsid) condition it is all the more (so); thus the condition becomes void (yabtul) and the relinquishment is valid (yasihh). Commentary: And it is not connected the relinquishment of the right of shuf'ah with a valid condition, then with an invalid one it is even more so; thus the condition becomes void and the relinquishment is valid. Explanation: An invalid condition is one that mentions property (mal), and one that does not mention property is a valid condition. Example: The shafi' says to the mushtari, 'I have relinquished my right of shuf'ah on the condition that the seller (ba'i') does not demand the price from me.' Obviously, since the shafi' is not taking the property, how can the ba'i' or mushtari demand the price from him? In summary, this condition is valid. If the shafi' says, 'I have relinquished my right on the condition that you give me one thousand rupees,' this is an invalid condition. Now understand the meaning of the text: He says that the relinquishment of the right of shuf'ah is not connected to any condition, whether valid or not; rather, its relinquishment is connected to his statement, 'I have relinquished my right.' The author said: When relinquishment is not connected to a valid condition, then with an invalid condition it is all the more so. In any case, when this is done, what happens? The answer: the condition becomes void, meaning the consideration must be returned, and the relinquishment is valid, meaning that what he relinquished of his right is relinquished, but he must return the consideration.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the act of relinquishing the right of shuf'ah is independent of any condition attached to it. The type is a ruling with rational proof. The author states that the validity of the relinquishment is not contingent upon any condition, whether the condition is valid (jaa'iz) or invalid (fasid). The commentary explains that a condition involving money is invalid; one not involving money is valid (e.g., not demanding the price). In all cases, the relinquishment itself takes effect immediately, but if the condition is invalid, the condition is void and any consideration must be returned. The key point is that the isqat (relinquishment) is a unilateral act that works independently; conditions do not affect its validity, only the validity of the condition itself. This ruling prevents the abuse of attaching invalid conditions to circumvent the prohibition of selling shuf'ah.

Key Terms
اسقاط (isqat): Relinquishment or dropping of a right – here specifically the right of shuf'ah.
شرط جائز (shart jaa'iz): A valid condition that does not involve a financial transaction, e.g., not demanding the price.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): An invalid condition that involves a financial exchange (e.g., payment for relinquishment).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling separates the validity of relinquishing shuf'ah from any attached condition; the isqat stands while an invalid condition is void and any consideration must be returned.

Selling the Right of Shuf'ah Is Invalid
Ruling on selling the right of shuf'ah as an invalid transaction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling the right of shuf'ah and explain why it is invalid.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is a right to acquire ownership, not property – selling it is void, and any payment must be returned.

This lesson extends the previous ruling on relinquishing shuf'ah for consideration. Just as a shafi' cannot take payment to drop his right, he also cannot sell the right itself. The reason is the same: shuf'ah is not a tradeable asset; it is merely a right (haqq) to step into a sale. Any transaction that treats it as mal is void ab initio.

Guided Path
1
Recall the prior ruling
Remember that relinquishing shuf'ah for a payment is invalid because shuf'ah is not property. This ruling was established in the previous passage.
2
Identify the new case
Now consider the scenario where the shafi' sells his right of shuf'ah outright to another person for a price. This is different from simply waiving it; it is a bilateral contract of sale.
3
Apply the same principle
The underlying principle is that shuf'ah is a right (haqq) to acquire ownership, not a property (mal) that can be sold. Since the subject matter of the sale is not valid mal, the contract is void.
4
Determine the consequence
The sale is null (batil) and any payment received becomes unlawful (ghasb). The amount must be returned to the buyer, and the right of shuf'ah remains with the original shafi'.
This is the same consequence as relinquishing for consideration.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

It is stated that here too the same previous ruling applies: the shuf'ah becomes void, and the amount he received must be returned, and the reason is the same as passed before.

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to the direct sale of the right of shuf'ah. The type is a ruling statement. It states that just as relinquishing shuf'ah for consideration is invalid, selling the right outright is also invalid. The shafi' cannot treat shuf'ah as a commodity to be sold. If he does, the sale is void and any payment must be returned. The reasoning is identical: shuf'ah is not a property right that can be traded; it is merely a right to acquire ownership. Therefore, any transaction treating it as an asset is null.

Established vs Non-Established Rights: Shuf'ah, Qisas, Talaq, Itq
Compares shuf'ah to qisas, talaq, and itq to explain why compensation is allowed there but not in shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between an established (mutaqarrir) and a non-established (ghayr mustaqir) right, and apply the Hanafi rule that only established rights can be exchanged for compensation.

Core Idea
A right that remains unchanged after sulh cannot be sold; only a right that creates a new benefit can be compensated.

This passage addresses a critical objection in Hanafi fiqh: if both shuf'ah and qisas are non-property rights, why is compensation allowed for qisas but not for shuf'ah? The answer hinges on a subtle classification: established (mutaqarrir) versus non-established (ghayr mustaqir) rights. Understanding this distinction clarifies not only shuf'ah and qisas but also the validity of khul' (divorce for compensation) and emancipation for a price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
The hypothetical objector argues that since both shuf'ah and qisas are non-property rights, they should be treated equally: if compensation is allowed for qisas, it should also be allowed for shuf'ah.
This is a classic qiyas (analogy) argument based on the common attribute of being 'non-property'.
2
State the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response rejects the analogy by introducing a new criterion: whether the right is established (mutaqarrir) or not. Qisas is mutaqarrir; shuf'ah is not.
The key is that 'non-property' is not the relevant attribute; rather, it is 'established in the subject'.
3
Understand the Criterion for Mutaqarrir
A right is mutaqarrir if, after a sulh (settlement), the subject (mahall) undergoes a change. In qisas, the killer's blood was licit (mubah al-dam) and after sulh, 'ismah (inviolability) is created in him – a new benefit. In shuf'ah, the property ownership does not change; the purchaser remains owner.
The change in the subject creates a new 'benefit' that can be sold.
4
Apply to Talaq and Itq
Khul' (divorce for compensation) and emancipation for a price are both valid because the husband/master has an established ownership (milk) in the wife/slave. Taking compensation for that established property right is valid.
This reinforces the principle: ownership (milk) is always established and can be exchanged.
5
Contrast with Shuf'ah
In shuf'ah, the shafi' has only a potential right to take the property. No change occurs in the property or its owner after a sulh; the owner simply pays nothing happens. Hence, it is ghayr mustaqir and cannot be compensated.
The shafi' cannot create a new benefit for the purchaser; thus, selling the right is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف القصاص لانه حق متقرر وبخلاف الطلاق والعتاق لانه اعتياض عن ملك في المحل
ترجمہ: بخلاف قصاس کے اسلئے کہ قصاص ایسا حق ہے جو ثابت و متقر ر ہے اور بخلاف طلاق وعتناق کے اسلئے کہ یہ عوض لینا ہے محل کے اندر ملکیت کا۔ تشریح یہاں اعتراض وارد ہو رہا تھا کہ جیسے حق شفعہ مال نہیں ہے ایسے ہی حق قصاص بھی مال نہیں ہے تو جیسے حق قصاص کا عوض لینا صحیح ہے ایسے ہی حق شفعہ کا عوض لینا بھی صحیح ہونا چاہئے؟ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ حق شفعہ حق منتظر نہیں ہے اور حق قصاص حق منتظر ر ہے اور حق مقر ر کا عوض لینا صحیح ہے اور غیر منتظر ر کا عوض لینا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ منتظر راور غیر مستقر کی پہچان یہ ہے کہ جہاں مصالحت سے پہلے اور بعد میں محل میں حکما تغیر ہو جائے وہ منتظر رہے ورنہ غیر مقرر ہے۔ مثلا مصالحت سے پہلے قاتل مباح الدم تھا اور مصالحت کے بعد اس کے اندر عصمت پیدا ہو گئی تو چونکہ من لۂ القصاص یعنی ولی نے قاتل کے اندر عصمت پیدا کر دی اس وجہ سے عصمت کا عوض لینا اس کیلئے صحیح ہے اور حق شفعہ میں مشتری مبیع کا مالک ہو چکا ہے۔ مصالحت سے پہلے ہی اور مصالحت کے بعد بھی وہی ملکیت برقرار ہے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ حق غیر منقر ر ہے جس کا عوض لینا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر شوہر اپنی بیوی کو مال کے بدلہ طلاق دے اور آقا مال کے بدلہ غلام کو آزاد کرے تو دونوں عوض لینا صحیح ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اس کا حق متقر ر ہونا ظاہر ہے اور شوہر اور آقا دونوں کو کل کے اندر ملکیت حاصل ہے اپنی اس ملک کا عوض لینا صحیح ہے۔
Contrary to qisas, because it is an established right (haqq mutaqarrir), and contrary to talaq and itq, because it is taking compensation for ownership in the property (mahall). Commentary: An objection arose: just as the right of shuf'ah is not property, similarly the right of qisas is not property. So why is taking compensation for qisas valid but not for shuf'ah? The answer: The right of shuf'ah is not an established right (mutaqarrir), while the right of qisas is an established right. Taking compensation for an established right is valid, but for a non-established right it is not valid. The sign of an established (mutaqarrir) vs non-established (ghayr mustaqir) right is: if after the sulh there is a change in the subject (mahall), it is mutaqarrir; otherwise not. For example, before the sulh, the killer had mubah al-dam (his blood was licit), and after the sulh, 'ismah (inviolability) was created in him. Since the guardian (wali) of qisas created 'ismah in the killer, taking compensation for that 'ismah is valid. In shuf'ah, the purchaser already owned the property before the sulh, and after the sulh the same ownership remains; thus it is ghayr mustaqir, and taking compensation is not valid. Similarly, if a husband divorces his wife for compensation (khul') and a master frees his slave for compensation, both are valid because the right is established: the husband and master have ownership (milk) in the subject, and taking compensation for that ownership is valid.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection by comparing shuf'ah to qisas, talaq (khul'), and itq (emancipation). The type is an inter-madhhab or intra-school dispute (though here it is a rational objection). The objector argues that since both shuf'ah and qisas are non-property rights, if compensation is allowed for qisas it should be allowed for shuf'ah. The Hanafi response distinguishes between established (mutaqarrir) and non-established (ghayr mustaqir) rights. Qisas is established because the guardian has power over the killer's life; after a sulh, the killer gains 'ismah, which is a new benefit. Thus, compensation is for that new 'ismah. In shuf'ah, the purchaser's ownership does not change; the shafi' merely has a potential right. Similarly, in talaq and itq, the husband and master have actual ownership (milk) in the wife and slave, which is an established property right, so taking compensation is valid. This clarifies that shuf'ah is a weaker, non-established right, hence cannot be exchanged for money.

Key Terms
حق متقرر (haqq mutaqarrir): An established right that is fixed in the subject and can be exchanged for compensation.
حق غير متقرر (haqq ghayr mutaqarrir): A non-established right that is not fixed in the subject; taking compensation for it is invalid.
عصمت ('ismah): Inviolability: protection from being killed; created in the killer after sulh in qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because qisas involves a life while shuf'ah involves property
B) Because qisas is an established right that creates a new benefit ('ismah) upon sulh, while shuf'ah does not
C) Because qisas is a criminal matter while shuf'ah is civil
D) Because the Qur'an explicitly allows compensation for qisas but not for shuf'ah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits compensation only for rights that are established (mutaqarrir), meaning the subject changes after the transaction, as in qisas, talaq, and itq, but not for shuf'ah because the property ownership remains unchanged.

Invalidity of Selling the Right of Pre-emption (Shuf'a)
Ruling with proof and analogical reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why selling the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) is invalid in Hanafi law, distinguish between settled and unsettled rights, and apply the same distinction to the case of kafala bi nafs.

Core Idea
An unsettled right cannot be sold for money — shuf'a is void because it is not property, unlike qisas which is a settled right.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author establishes a critical distinction between two types of rights: those that are settled (haqq mutaqarrir) and those that are not. This distinction determines whether a right can be exchanged for compensation. The ruling on selling the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) serves as the primary example, followed by analogical cases and a discussion of intra-Hanafi differences regarding surety for a person (kafala bi nafs).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its proof
Read the opening section. The ruling is that if a pre-emptor sells his right of shuf'a for money, the sale is void (batil) and the consideration must be returned. The reason is that the right of shuf'a is not property and is an unsettled right.
The phrase 'بطل الشفعة' (the pre-emption becomes void) is key.
2
Understand the distinction between settled and unsettled rights
The passage contrasts shuf'a with qisas. Qisas is a settled right because the killer's status changes from permissible blood to inviolability after settlement. In shuf'a, the buyer's ownership remains unchanged, making it unsettled. This distinction explains why qisas can be exchanged for compensation but shuf'a cannot.
The mark of a settled right is that the subject undergoes a legal change (تغير الحكم في المحل).
3
Apply the distinction to the analogical cases
The passage gives two analogies from family law: (1) a husband who gave his wife a choice (takhyir) later says 'choose me for a thousand'; (2) an impotent husband says to his wife 'give up the right to annul for a thousand'. In both, the option falls but no money is due. These show that an option (khiyar), like shuf'a, is an unsettled right that cannot be sold.
These analogies strengthen the ruling by showing consistent application of the principle.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on kafala bi nafs
The passage reports two narrations regarding surety for a person: one treats it like shuf'a (void, no consideration), another says it is not void and no consideration. Some scholars extend the second narration to shuf'a, but the majority limit it to kafala. The relied-upon position for shuf'a remains that the sale is void.
This step shows how usul al-hanafiyyah deals with conflicting narrations within the school.

كتاب الشفعة

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۳
ترجمہ اور اس کی نظیر جبکہ شوہر نے مخیرہ سے کہا کہ ہزار کے بدلہ میں مجھے کو اختیار کر لے یا عمنین نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ ہزار کے بدلہ میں ترک فسخ کو اختیار کرلے پس اس نے اختیار کر لیا تو خیار ساقط ہو گیا اور عوض ثابت نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حق شفعہ کی نظیر یہ مسائل ہیں کہ جہاں عوض بھی ثابت نہیں ہوتا اور خیار ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ کسی شخص نے اپنی عورت کو خیار دیتے ہوئے کہا اختاری نفسک جس کی تفصیل ہدایہ جلد ثانی میں گذر چکی ہے۔ اب شوہر نے خطرہ محسوس کیا کہ کہیں عورت اپنے نفس کو اختیار نہ کرلے اور طلاق بائن واقع ہو جائے اس خطرہ کے پیش نظر اس نے بیوی سے کہا کہ ہزار کے بدلہ میں تو مجھے ہی اختیار کر لے۔ عورت نے کر لیا تو عورت کا خیار ساقط ہو گیا اور ہزار روپے واجب نہ ہوں گے۔ عنین کی بیوی کو اختیار نسخ ملتا ہے جس کی تفصیل ہدایہ جلد ثانی میں گذر چکی ہے مگر شوہر نے اس سے کہا کہ تو نکاح فسخ نہ کر اور میں تجھے ہزار روپے دوں گا تو عورت نے فتح کو ترک کر دیا، اب بھی عورت کا خیار ختم ہو گیا اور عوض بھی باطل ہو گیا۔ یعنی یہ دونوں مسئلے حق شفعہ کی نظیر ہیں جن کی مثال یہ ہے کہ دھوبی کا کتان گھر کا نہ گھاٹ کا۔
كفالۃ بالنفس شفعہ کی طرح ہے یا نہیں
والكفالة بالنفس في هذا بمنزلة الشفعة في رواية وفى اخرى لا تبطل الكفالة ولا يجب المال وقيل هذا رواية في الشفعة وقيل هى فى الكفالة خاصة وقد عرف في موضعه.
ترجمہ اور کفالت بالنفس اس سلسلہ میں ( بطلان کفالت و عوض کے اندر ) ایک روایت کے مطابق شفعہ کے درجہ میں ہے اور دوسری روایت کے مطابق کفالت باطل نہیں ہوگی اور مال واجب نہ ہوگا اور کہا گیا کہ یہ روایت فقط کفالت کے اندر ہے اور اس کو پہچان لیا گیا ہے اس کے مقام میں۔ تشریح کسی شخص نے کسی کی جانی کفالت کی جس کو کفالت بالنفس کہتے ہیں جس کا مقصد یہ ہوتا ہے کہ کفیل اس شخص کو مکفول لڑ کے پاس حاضر کر دے پھر کفیل نے مکفول لہ سے کہا کہ تو ہزار روپے لے کر مجھے کفالت سے بری کر دے اس نے کر دیا اب کیا حکم ہے۔ تو فرمایا کہ اس کے اندر مختلف روایات ہیں۔ ایک روایت کے مطابق تو یہ شفعہ کے مثل ہے یعنی کفالت باطل اور عوض واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور دوسری روایت کے مطابق مال واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور نہ کفالت باطل ہوگی بعض مشائخ احناف نے کہا ہے کہ کفالت کے اندر جو ایک روایت ہے ایسی ہی ایک روایت شفعہ کے اندر بھی ہے یعنی شفعہ باطل نہ ہوگا اور عوض واجب نہ ہوگا۔ بعض مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ نہیں بلکہ یہ روایت فقط کفالت کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے شفعہ کے اندر نہیں ہے بلکہ وہاں تو وہی حکم اصلی ہے کہ عوض باطل اور شفعہ بھی باطل ہے۔ اس کے بعد مصنف نے فرمایا کہ اس مسئلہ کی تفصیلات اس کے مقام پر موجود ہیں یعنی مبسوط کے اندر۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume 13
It falls, but the consideration must be returned.
If the pre-emptor sold his right of pre-emption to someone, then too the right of pre-emption will become void. And similarly, if the pre-emptor sells his pre-emption for money... Translation: And similarly, if the pre-emptor sold his pre-emption, due to the reason we have mentioned. Book of Pre-emption.
Explanation: That is, just as it was not permissible for the pre-emptor to drop his right by taking consideration, similarly if the pre-emptor sold his right of pre-emption to someone, then what happens? He said that here too the same previous ruling applies, i.e., the pre-emption becomes void and the amount he received must be returned, and the proof is the same as passed before.
Ruling on analogizing the right of pre-emption to the right of retaliation (qisas): Contrary to qisas because it is a settled right, and contrary to divorce and emancipation because it is taking compensation for ownership in the subject matter. Translation: Contrary to qisas because qisas is a right that is established and settled, and contrary to divorce and emancipation because these are taking compensation for ownership in the subject matter.
Explanation: Here an objection was raised that just as the right of pre-emption is not property, similarly the right of qisas is not property. So just as taking compensation for the right of qisas is valid, similarly taking compensation for the right of pre-emption should be valid? He answered that the right of pre-emption is not a settled right, while the right of qisas is a settled right. Taking compensation for a settled right is valid, and taking compensation for an unsettled right is not valid. The distinguishing mark between a settled and unsettled right is: where before and after settlement, there is a legal change in the subject, that is settled; otherwise, it is unsettled.
For example, before settlement, the killer was of permissible blood, and after settlement, inviolability (isma) is established in him. Since the guardian (wali) of the right of qisas created inviolability in the killer, therefore taking compensation for that inviolability is valid for him. In the right of pre-emption, the buyer already owned the purchased property before the settlement, and the same ownership remains after the settlement. Hence, this is an unsettled right, for which taking compensation is not valid. Similarly, if a husband divorces his wife for money, or a master emancipates a slave for money, taking compensation is valid for both because their right is clearly settled, and both have ownership in the whole, so taking compensation for that ownership is valid.
Analogy for the right of pre-emption: And its analogy: when a husband says to a wife with a choice (mukhayyara): 'Choose me for a thousand,' or a man with impotence ('innin) says to his wife: 'Choose to give up dissolution for a thousand,' and she so chooses, then the option falls and the consideration is not established. Translation: And its analogy: when the husband says to the mukhayyara: 'Choose me for a thousand,' or the 'innin says to his wife: 'Choose to give up dissolution for a thousand,' and she chooses, then the option falls and the consideration is not established.
Explanation: The author of Hidayah says that the analogy for the right of pre-emption are these issues where the consideration is not established and the option falls. A man gave his wife a choice saying 'Choose yourself,' the details of which have passed in volume two of Hidayah. Now the husband felt the danger that perhaps the wife might choose herself and a final divorce might occur. In view of this danger, he said to his wife: 'Choose me for a thousand.' The wife chose; then the wife's option fell, and the thousand rupees are not obligatory. The wife of an 'innin has the option of annulment, whose details have passed in volume two of Hidayah. But the husband said to her: 'Do not annul the marriage, and I will give you a thousand rupees.' The wife then gave up annulment. Here too, the wife's option ended and the consideration became void. That is, both these issues are analogies for the right of pre-emption, whose example is: 'The washerman's cloth belongs neither to the house nor to the bank.'
Whether surety for a person (kafala bi nafs) is like pre-emption or not: And surety for a person in this matter is like pre-emption in one narration, and in another narration the surety does not become void and the money is not obligatory. And it has been said that this is a narration in pre-emption, and it has been said that it is specifically in surety, and it has been recognized in its place. Translation: And surety for a person in this matter (concerning voidability and consideration) is like pre-emption in one narration, and in another narration the surety does not become void and the money is not obligatory. And it has been said that this narration is also in pre-emption, and it has been said that it is specifically in surety, and it has been recognized in its place.
Explanation: A person gave surety for another person's presence (kafala bi nafs), whose purpose is that the surety brings the principal before the beneficiary. Then the surety said to the beneficiary: 'Take a thousand rupees and absolve me of the surety.' He did so. Now what is the ruling? He said that there are different narrations. According to one narration, it is like pre-emption, i.e., the surety is void and the consideration is not obligatory. According to another narration, the money is not obligatory and the surety is also not void. Some Hanafi scholars said that the narration which is in surety, a similar narration also exists in pre-emption, i.e., pre-emption is not void and the consideration is not obligatory. Some scholars said that no, rather this narration is specifically for surety and not for pre-emption; rather, there the original ruling is that the consideration is void and pre-emption is also void. After this, the author said that the details of this issue are present in its place, i.e., in Mabsoot.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling that selling the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) is invalid and the consideration must be returned. The commentator begins by reaffirming the ruling: just as it is impermissible for the pre-emptor to drop his right for compensation, similarly selling that right is void. The proof is the same as earlier: the right of shuf'a is not property. An objection is anticipated: why is taking compensation for qisas valid (since it is also not property) but not for shuf'a? The distinction is that qisas is a settled right (haqq mutaqarrir) because the subject (the killer) undergoes a legal change (from permissible blood to inviolability), whereas shuf'a is unsettled (ghayr mustaqirr) because the buyer's ownership is unchanged before and after the transaction. Similarly, divorce for compensation (khula') and emancipation for money are valid because the husband and master have full ownership. The passage then gives two analogies from family law: (1) a husband who gave his wife a general choice (takhyir) later tells her 'choose me for a thousand'; if she accepts, the option falls but no payment is due. (2) A wife of an impotent husband (who had the right to annul) is told to give up that right for money; if she agrees, the option falls but no money is owed. These show that an option (which is a right not yet settled) cannot be exchanged for money validly. Finally, the passage discusses kafala bi nafs (surety for a person). There are two narrations: one treats it like shuf'a (void, no consideration), another says it is not void and no consideration. Some scholars extend the second narration to shuf'a, but the preferred view is that the second narration is specific to kafala. The details are in greater works like al-Mabsoot.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): The right of pre-emption in property sales, allowing a co-owner or neighbor to purchase the sold share, which is an unsettled right (ghayr mustaqirr) not considered property.
حق متقرر (haqq mutaqarrir): A settled right that is established and whose subject undergoes a legal change upon settlement, such as qisas where the killer's status changes from permissible blood to inviolability.
كفالة بالنفس (kafala bi nafs): Surety for a person, i.e., guaranteeing that the principal will appear before the beneficiary. It is a right similar in nature to shuf'a but subject to differing narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is taking compensation for the right of qisas valid in Hanafi law, but taking compensation for the right of shuf'a is not?
A) Because qisas is property while shuf'a is not.
B) Because qisas is a settled right (haqq mutaqarrir) while shuf'a is unsettled (ghayr mustaqirr).
C) Because shuf'a involves immovable property while qisas involves the person.
D) Because the Quran explicitly allows compensation for qisas but not for shuf'a.

Key Takeaway
An unsettled right (ghayr mustaqirr) cannot be sold for money; any transaction to sell such a right is void and any consideration must be returned.
